They will be announced as soon as they arrive at the ministry. (Special dispatch, 22nd)

Subordinate District Party Departments Temporarily Exercise the Power to Supervise County Administration

(Nanjing) The Central Executive Committee states that county party departments have the power to supervise the policy guidelines and performance of county governments. Currently, county party departments have not been universally established in various places. There are only subordinate district party departments in some places. The organization of these subordinate district party departments is different from that of county party departments, but they are the sole party organs of the entire county. They should still be allowed to exercise the power to supervise the policy guidelines and performance of county governments. According to the resolution of the Central Supervisory Committee, the Central Standing Committee has stipulated that in counties where county party departments have not been established, the subordinate district party departments may temporarily exercise the power of supervision. The provincial party departments have been notified to comply, and the National Government has ordered the provincial governments to comply. (Special dispatch, 22nd)

Current Events Commentary

New Lineup of European Gold Standard Countries - Su

France, the Netherlands, Belgium, Italy, and Switzerland. These are the only five major gold standard countries remaining in the world today. How can they stand firm amidst this raging tide of currency inflation and remain unchanged in the face of gold? Surely many scholars will consider this a miracle today. However, if we examine it carefully, we realize that their intention to "play the game" is actually no different in essence from countries like the United Kingdom, the United States, and Japan, which are vigorously pursuing currency inflation. Although they nominally do not follow in the footsteps of the United Kingdom, the United States, and Japan, they are actually doing exactly the same thing, using the maintenance of the "gold standard" as a weapon to compete for markets. Such methods are indeed identical.

The five major gold standard countries, France, the Netherlands, Belgium, Italy, and Switzerland, recently signed a protocol in Brussels, Belgium, based on a proposal by Belgian Foreign Minister Jaspar. Three points in the protocol are worth noting. First, reconfirming the policy of maintaining the current gold content of the currencies of the respective countries. Second, regarding the exchange of goods between the respective countries, it is hoped that the actual trade volume in the one-year period after July 1, 1933, will be used as the basis for a 10% increase. Third, matters concerning tourism and transportation will be discussed after a detailed report is prepared. From these three points, we already know that these five major gold standard countries are attempting to move towards a higher level of economic groupism based on several "like-minded" countries. What does this signify?

Everyone knows that since 1929, almost every country in the world, except for Soviet Russia, which is still able to increase national production based on its two five-year plans, has been in a state of extreme difficulty. Therefore, the contraction of trade volume and the reduction of capital profits have become the fundamental reasons driving those great powers to engage in more intense economic warfare. Under this situation, economic units such as the "Sterling Bloc," the "Dollar Bloc," and the "Gold Standard Bloc" have emerged. Based on this principle of "joining forces with the majority of countries," the general powers have gradually begun to raise their heads again from their declining fortunes. If the five major countries want to fight further, they certainly cannot escape this method. This is the first point expressed in the protocol of the five major gold standard countries. Second, the protocol of the five major gold standard countries also expresses a counterattack against the currency inflation movements of the United Kingdom and the United States. Under the silver movement, the exchange rates for gold standard countries have become lower and lower day by day. Furthermore, the economic blocs of the United Kingdom and the United States are using the effects of currency inflation to stimulate production upwards and to expand markets through dumping. This is an even greater threat to gold standard countries. Therefore, it is necessary to reorganize this front in order to counter the offensive of the United Kingdom and the United States.

Finally, the recent protocol of the five major gold standard countries also indicates an even more important significance, which is that the sharpness of economic warfare has deepened even further. If the actual trade volume among the five major gold standard countries is to be expanded by 10%, it will only be possible by further expanding the application of quantitative import controls. Now, not only trade is subject to such severe restrictions, but also travel and transportation must be subject to control policies. How can such a nerve-wracking battle plan not make people nervous? The five major gold standard countries are giving such an answer to other related powers. We cannot but pay extra attention to their future.

Changsha Restoration Commemoration

(Changsha) On the 22nd, the local restoration anniversary was commemorated. He Jian delivered a speech, hoping to continue the revolutionary spirit of the martyrs, emphasize spiritual construction, complete the revolution. Veteran comrades who participated in the 1911 Revolution, Wang Fenwu and Wen Muxi, reported the process of responding to the Wuhan Uprising and then dispersed. (22nd Special Dispatch)

Closing of the Second Plenary Congress of the Air Force Special Party Department

Publication of a Declaration of the Congress

Determination of Future Struggle Guidelines

(Nanchang) The Second All-Army Representative Congress of the Air Force Special Party Department was held at the Nanchang Aircraft Shed Factory on the 20th. The opening ceremony and the first meeting have been reported in yesterday's news. It is now learned that the meeting continued with the second session at 8:00 a.m. on the 21st, and resolved many important cases. The third session continued at 2:00 p.m. to elect executive and supervisory committee members. Under the supervision of Central Supervisor Ding Chao Wu, Jiang Jianren, Xu Hongtao, Xie Tingfan, Zhou Xiuzhong, Zhang Shaowu, Long Tao, and Zhang Guowei were elected as executive committee members. Hou Balun, Huang Zhengyu, and Ye Xiangxian were elected as alternate executive committee members. Cao Baoqing, Huang Bingheng, Mao Bangchu, Zhou Yurous, and Shen Kaihuan were elected as supervisory committee members. Hu Guangjin and Shen Dexie were elected as alternate supervisory committee members. After the election, the congress declaration was discussed and unanimously approved, followed by a discussion of temporary motions (omitted). The meeting adjourned at 5:00 p.m. The declaration of the congress is as follows: Declaration of the Second All-Army Representative Congress of the Air Force Special Party Department. In order to review past work and promote future party affairs, this Special Party Department specially convened the Second All-Army Representative Congress in Nanchang on the 20th of this month, which concluded on the 22nd. A total of 78 representatives attended and more than 30 proposals were discussed. The spirit of the congress was to be fast and practical, and the venue presented unlimited vitality. Now that the task of the congress has been completed, we have determined the future struggle guidelines for our country based on the needs of the environment. The mission of our air force is to take "avenging humiliation and revenge" as the greatest goal. We recognize the perilous nature of the national environment and the importance of our own responsibilities. In the future progress of air force construction, we must lead all air force party members to work hard in many aspects. (1) We must eliminate all bad old habits and old concepts, cultivate new life and new living, so that the body of the air force will not be tempted or eroded by external objects, and become a healthy person at the forefront of the times. (2) We must base on the principle of self-reliance and self-improvement, and not rely on external forces for development. Although it cannot be completely achieved recently, we must gradually seek self-reliant construction. (3) We must complete the plan of "internal pacification before resisting foreign aggression", and do our best to assist all armies in thoroughly suppressing the Red bandits, eliminating rebellion, and seeking the true unification of the country. (4) We must absolutely obey the command of the revolutionary leader Chairman Chiang Kai-shek, undertake the arduous task of completing the second phase of the National Revolution in China, and restore the status of the Chinese nation. (5) We must engage in rigorous self-training. Training is the vitality for our air force to eliminate the old and bring forth the new. We must use countless trials and tribulations to bring the technology, physique, character, and spirit of our military personnel to the highest peak, and make each of them a healthy cell. (6) We must party-ize the air force. If the air force is not party-ized, the party's revolutionary spirit will have no place to be placed in the air force. We must have a living and revolutionary-spirited air force, we must party-ize it. (7) We must urgently expand and enrich the air force for the purpose of self-defense in the Second World War, and never let today's air force repeat the mistakes of the Sino-Japanese War navy. (8) We must unite sincerely and take love and mutual assistance as the only moral concept, eliminate the bad habit of non-cooperation and factionalism, and through the unity within the air force, we must jointly seek the common life and death of the army, navy, and air force, so as to obtain the greatest guarantee of victory in the decisive battle against foreign aggression. In short, based on the above-mentioned common beliefs, this conference vows to supervise and lead all air force personnel to complete it in the shortest period of time, so as to live up to the painstaking efforts of the revolutionary leader who founded the air force, and to satisfy the most sincere and enthusiastic expectations of compatriots and comrades across the country. Secretariat of the Second All-Army Representative Congress of the Air Force Special Party Department. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 22nd)

The Problem of Connecting the Yuehan and Jinghan Railways

(Nanjing) A person in charge of the Ministry of Railways talked about the problem of connecting the Yuehan and Pinghan Railways. There are three methods for river transportation between the towns of Wuhan: one is to build a bridge across the river, the second is to dig a tunnel under the river, and the third is to use ferries to travel between the two towns. Each of the three has its advantages and disadvantages. Building a bridge is expensive, but the trains run easily. Digging a tunnel is a huge project, but there is no special danger. As for building ferries, it is easy to do, but the engines must be replaced from time to time, which is not a permanent solution. According to the current national economic situation, ferries are the most reasonable. (22nd Special Dispatch)

The Ministry of Railways Plans to Build the Sichuan-Han Railway

(Hankou) According to transportation circles, Sichuan has abundant products, but due to inconvenient transportation, the local products cannot be sold to the outside world. The Sichuan-Han Railway was suspended due to the European War, and the government has not been able to promote it for more than 20 years. It is now reported that the ministry plans to raise funds and start construction. Recently, it plans to send airplanes over Hanzhong into Sichuan to observe the roadbed along the way, so as to start planning everything. (22nd Central News Agency Dispatch)

Whether he will take office is still under consideration. In terms of serving his hometown, he cannot refuse. In terms of the complex situation in the county, he is afraid that his talent is not enough to handle it. County administration is a miniature of national politics. If there is something that can be done, he would dare not be afraid of difficulties. As for all reform views, they cannot be discussed until the entire situation is understood. Even if they are understood, he will not make grand gestures to avoid being accused of empty promises. (22nd Special Dispatch)

Yu Hanmou and Li Yangjing Return to Defense

(Hong Kong) Yu Hanmou, accompanied by Zhang Da and Li Hanhun, set off on a Yuehan special train on the 21st and arrived in Shaoguan at 4:00 a.m. on the 22nd. Shocking News From the British Press: Japan and Germany Conclude Secret Agreement

Japan Exchanges Soybeans for German Munitions

(London) The Daily Mail reports that Japan and Germany secretly concluded a very important commercial agreement six weeks ago. The agreement stipulates that Japan will exchange a very large quantity of soybeans for German chemicals, explosives, machine guns, and aircraft engines. Soybeans can be used for human and animal food, and Germany will import one million tons per year. Another agreement stipulates that Germany will send 500 aviators and engineers to Japan by 1935. (22nd Havas Dispatch)

Reform Plan for Japanese-Controlled Puppet Organizations - New Official System

(Tokyo) The Bureau of Legislation has drafted a new official system for the reform plan for the organizations in Manchuria. The essential points of the draft are as follows: (1) The Affairs Bureau for Manchuria will be directly under the management of the Prime Minister, managing the affairs of the South Manchuria Affairs Bureau. The President will be an appointed official, and the Vice President will be a appointed official. (2) Although the President of the South Manchuria Affairs Bureau does not have the qualifications stipulated in the appointment orders for diplomats, consuls, and secretaries, he may be appointed as a counselor to the Embassy in Manchuria while in office. (3) Although the army officers who are the commanders of the Kwantung Army Gendarmerie do not have the qualifications stipulated in the appointment orders for civil officials, they may be appointed as ministers of the Colonization Department while in office. (4) The South Manchuria Affairs Bureau will be established within the Embassy in Manchuria. The Ambassador Plenipotentiary to Manchuria will be under the supervision of the Prime Minister, managing the affairs of the South Manchuria Affairs Bureau, but foreign affairs matters will be under the supervision of the Minister of Foreign Affairs. (5) The Kwantung Office will be established in Dairen. (6) The Minister of Colonization will manage the affairs of the Governor-General of Korea, the Governor-General of Taiwan, the Karafuto Agency, and the South Seas Agency, except for the Kwantung Office. (22nd Dentsu Dispatch)

The UK and the US Unanimously Oppose Japan's Increasing Naval Ratio

It is rumored that the UK intends to accept the total tonnage system

Preliminary UK-Japan talks begin today

(London) At the time of the naval talks, the UK will probably try its best to oppose Japan or other countries' motions to change the current warship ratio system and replace it with a total tonnage system, because the total tonnage system will be very unfavorable to the UK. American experts also said that after the total tonnage system is implemented, the United States will concentrate all its efforts on building large battleships, heavy cruisers, and aircraft carriers, which is opposed by both the UK and Japan. Therefore, the London Times and the Observer have recently published articles saying that the UK may accept the total tonnage system to resolve the difficulties of the ratio problem, which surprised everyone. British naval authorities said that no matter what the meaning of this argument is, it cannot show that the UK can allow Japan to increase its ratio. It is said that the UK has long planned to add high-speed cruisers. It is heard that Prime Minister MacDonald confirmed in mid-July that the UK will increase the number of cruisers by 50 to 70 after the expiration of the Washington and London treaties. However, if the United States specializes in building giant ships under the total tonnage system, the UK will not be limited by the situation and build unnecessary warships. (21st National Dispatch)

Contents of Japanese Proposal

(Tokyo) According to Japanese newspaper reports, the atmosphere in London is now better than before, and there is hope of concluding a new treaty to replace the Washington Naval Treaty. Officials here believe that the progress of all matters depends on the results of the preliminary UK-Japan talks starting tomorrow. Japan will decide its own attitude after it is sure of the attitudes of the UK and the US. However, according to Japanese newspaper reports, Japan's naval policy is based on the following points: (1) Military equipment must be sufficient for defense needs and ensure national defense security, but not enough to attack people. (2) Abolish the 5:5:3 ratio. (3) Abolish offensive weapons such as aircraft carriers and reduce the tonnage of battleships. (4) Retain defensive weapons such as submarines. (5) Abolish the Washington Naval Treaty, and it is even better to have joint action by the signatory countries. (6) Conclude a new treaty based on the principles of equality and fairness, and stipulate the total tonnage. It is heard that methods are currently being discussed to publish Japan's proposal in London and Tokyo at the same time. (22nd Reuters Dispatch)

British Opinions are Divided into Two Factions

(London) The outline of Japan's demands on naval issues has been explained to the press by Rear Admiral Yamamoto. When the individual talks between the UK and Japan officially begin, Rear Admiral Yamamoto will also explain in detail. These talks are scheduled to be held at 11:30 tomorrow morning, chaired by Prime Minister MacDonald. Currently, British public opinion on the various points requested by the Japanese navy has two different opinions: one is that political figures are eager to avoid naval arms competition, and their attitude is inclined to compromise; the other is that the naval department firmly opposes any concessions. In addition, the United States also expresses hostility to the ambitions of the Japanese navy, which will make the British naval department more determined, because the people in the department, in addition to their views on technical issues, also have the political view that the Anglo-Saxon nation should maintain its solidarity in the Pacific, and will therefore become more and more eloquent. (22nd Havas Dispatch)

(Tokyo) When the preliminary talks in London begin, the Imperial Government will propose a new disarmament policy to the UK and the US, and move towards concluding a new disarmament treaty. However, whether or not the new disarmament policy proposed this time will be announced, the foreign and naval authorities have already agreed on the policy, and the decision is as follows:

(1) When inviting preliminary talks, the British government said that these talks would be conducted individually and the content would not be made public. Therefore, the Imperial Government will consult with the British government when announcing the disarmament policy. (2) When it is deemed necessary to announce the disarmament policy, it should be announced in London and Tokyo at the same time. (22nd Dentsu Dispatch)

(Tokyo) The naval negotiations between Japan and the UK are scheduled to begin tomorrow (the 23rd). The Japanese representatives plan to first present Japan's disarmament plan and explain the reasons for the abolition of the Washington Treaty. The Japanese government's disarmament plan will be released simultaneously in London and Tokyo on the 23rd. (22nd Jiji Dispatch)

Japanese Side Declares That the Conclusion of Non-Aggression Treaty Has Not Been Considered

(Tokyo) Recently, rumors have been spreading both inside and outside Japan that Japan has seen through the breakdown of the Disarmament Conference and will propose to the UK and the US the conclusion of a non-aggression treaty after the breakdown. The task of Ambassador Hirota, the former ambassador to Italy, representing the Minister of Foreign Affairs, is also in this regard. However, at this time when the preliminary disarmament talks are about to begin, fearing that this rumor will be used as a tool for containment, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs will issue an unofficial statement today, denying this claim, saying that Japan is determined to break away from the shackles of the Washington Treaty after the end of 1936, and is also determined to propose a new disarmament plan in this preliminary disarmament talk, hoping to conclude a new maritime treaty. It is rumored that it intends to propose to the UK and the US the conclusion of a political treaty after the breakdown of the conference, but the Japanese government has no such preparations. (22nd China United Dispatch)

Sino-Soviet Negotiations Continue on the Sale of the Chinese Eastern Railway

Hirota Demands Withdrawal of New Conditions

Russian Representative Cables Moscow for Instructions

(Tokyo) Regarding the illegal negotiations for the Chinese Eastern Railway, since the meeting between the Russian Ambassador Yurenev and Foreign Minister Hirota on the 15th of this month, the negotiations were again on the verge of collapse due to the new conditions proposed by the Russian side. Afterwards, as a result of consultations between the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the Ministries of Finance and Commerce, it was decided to reject the new proposal from the Russian side. Foreign Minister Hirota then invited the Russian ambassador to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs at 1:30 PM today to demand the withdrawal of the new conditions by the Russian side. It is reported that Hirota's attitude today was quite firm. (Hualian Telegram, 22nd)

(Tokyo) Soviet Ambassador Yurenev visited Foreign Minister Hirota at 1:30 PM on the 22nd to continue negotiations on the sale of the Chinese Eastern Railway. Regarding the detailed items that Foreign Minister Hirota had presented to the Soviet Union twice on the 5th and 15th of this month, the ambassador avoided answering immediately and agreed to request instructions from his government again. The meeting lasted for one and a half hours before he left. The main points of this negotiation are recorded on the left:

(1) The issue of payment methods: The Japanese side insisted that the guarantee by the Japanese banking group was sufficient. The ambassador argued that the guarantee for current funds and commodity prices should be in the form of obtaining public bonds. (2) The issue of transfer: Although the Japanese side agreed to remove the consulate and its affiliated items, it did not agree that hospitals, clubs, libraries, and other items should be excluded. The ambassador argued that all items affiliated with the consulate should be owned by them. (3) The issue of the list of lending targets: The Japanese side insisted that the list of lending targets after March was absolutely necessary. The ambassador said that the portion submitted in March of this year was sufficient, and the current lending status was already known to the "Manchukuo" side. (4) The issue of the period for commodity payment: The Japanese side advocated for three and a half years, while the Soviet side advocated for two and a half years. (5) The issue of treaty preparation: When an agreement is reached, the full text of the treaty should be prepared in Japanese, Russian, and "Manchukuo" languages. If there is any doubt about the wording, the Japanese version should be the basis. Both sides expressed agreement on this point. (Rilian Telegram, 22nd)

Hungary and Poland Prepare for Friendly Negotiations and Treaty Signing

Hungarian Prime Minister Returns Home via Vienna

Polish Government Awards the Order of the White Eagle

The current result of this meeting is to establish a Polish-Hungarian cultural and scientific agreement, following the precedent of Poland and Yugoslavia. Negotiations will be held again soon to conclude a consular treaty and an agreement on travel. In addition, a committee will be organized to promote trade between the two countries. (Havas Telegram, 22nd)

(Warsaw) Hungarian Prime Minister Gömbös arrived here the night before last and visited key figures in Polish politics. A public statement was issued tonight, expressing mutual sympathy. However, it stated that the current result of Gömbös' visit to Warsaw is only the establishment of a cultural and scientific agreement, similar to the one concluded between Poland and Yugoslavia. Therefore, Gömbös' visit is only to demonstrate mutual willingness in a friendly manner. Gömbös acknowledged that Poland "should occupy a position among the world's great powers," while Polish Prime Minister Kozłowski said, "All international solutions that do not take into account the economic interlocking relationships of Central and Eastern Europe are in vain." Accomplices Continue to Be Apprehended in France Regarding the Marseille Assassination

Leader of Terrorist Group Under Interrogation

Extradition to France Will Take Time

(Paris) According to reports, another person has been arrested in Dieppe (on the sleeve coast in northern France), named Altug Keviczky, one of the accomplices in the Marseille murder case. Born in 1889, he carries a Hungarian passport, on which the name written is Altug Keviczky, one of the most dangerous members of the terrorist group "Vaszcsalisták." He has committed many crimes. In Austria, he attacked international trains heading to Yugoslavia. He had two accomplices during the train robbery, one was Pospisil, who was arrested in France for the Marseille case, and the other was Kvaternik, who was arrested in Italy for the Marseille case. Altug Keviczky was sentenced to ten months in prison. Recently, he was in London. The French police specially negotiated with the British Central Detective Agency "Scotland Yard," and he was deported. He was arrested when he crossed the sea to France. After investigating what he did between December 14, 1933, and October 1934, it will be clear. (Havas Telegram, 22nd)

(Turin, Italy) Italian police have consistently refused to announce details of the arrest of Pavelić and Kvaternik, the leaders of the Croatian terrorist group. The examining magistrate of Marseille, France, has requested that the two be extradited to France for trial. It will likely take several weeks before this can be done. Although Italian law stipulates that the crime of murdering foreign heads of state and politicians is sufficient grounds for extradition, it must be approved by the Court of Appeal before the Minister of Justice can grant permission. This procedure takes a lot of time. According to reports, Pavelić and Kvaternik hid their identities and lived in Milan and Turin. After receiving a radio message from the French police, the Italian police arrested the two within 48 hours. Their swiftness is admirable. (Havas Telegram, 21st)

(Turin, Italy) Italian authorities interrogated Pavelić and Kvaternik, the leaders of the Croatian terrorist group. As a result, they completely denied participating in the Marseille murder case, saying that they had not issued any orders, had not been to France for many years, and had never met the people arrested in France. Declaration by the Gold Bloc Causes Currency Price Fluctuations

(London) The declaration by the Gold Bloc to maintain the gold content of their currencies is the reason for the rise in the prices of the French franc and the US dollar this morning. Italy's paper money reserve is now only slightly higher than 40% of the statutory amount because Italy is exporting gold to offset its trade deficit. Today, the Financial Times stated that any European country that abandons gold will join the Sterling Bloc, and the result may be that Europe will restore the gold standard under the Sterling flag. China is currently trying to join the Sterling Bloc, following the steps of Japan, Argentina, and Brazil. Hurricane on the US West Coast

Ships Lost, Traffic Disrupted

Philippines Hit Again for the Second Time

(Seattle) This area was hit by a hurricane tonight. The hurricane's speed is 95 miles per hour. Shipping and telegraph and telephone communications have suffered heavy losses. Airlines have also been suspended. It is reported that 11 people have died, two of whom died from touching fallen power lines. The cargo ship Fullerida has run aground. It sent out a distress call at 9:30 AM this morning. The ship has 32 crew members. The President Madison drifted from its moorings in the harbor. The steamer Harvest was sunk in a collision, but 20 crew members swam to shore and were rescued. The steamers Aleutian and North Haven were also damaged in collisions. In addition, the steamer Virginia was blown away, but all 30 of its sailors were rescued. One fishing boat had five people fall into the water, but only two were rescued. In addition, three fishermen drowned. (National Telegram, 21st)

(Manila) The last typhoon in Manila killed a total of 80 people. Just as they were catching their breath, it is known that southern Manila was hit by a hurricane again on Saturday and Thursday. Although Manila was the first to bear the brunt of the typhoon last week, it was spared this time. The hurricane swept from the sea towards Camarines Sur province late Saturday night. The wind was strongest at noon on Sunday. Traffic in the affected provinces was disrupted. There are few reports from the disaster area, but it is reported that at least four people died in Naga. At the same time, it is estimated that property losses have exceeded one million pesos. The Philippine Senate today passed a million-peso typhoon relief fund. The bill has now been submitted to the Governor for signature. The bill has already been passed by the House of Representatives. (National Telegram, 22nd)

Japanese Students Banned from Dance Halls

Red-Light Districts Suddenly Become Desolate

(Tokyo) It has only been half a month since the police department strictly prohibited students from entering the red-light districts, and many cafes, taverns, dance halls, and other places have been hit hard. In particular, businesses in student districts have suffered a great impact. If they continue to maintain their businesses in this way, they will decline, and waiting for bankruptcy is obvious. Therefore, many merchants in the same industry are now successively applying to the Metropolitan Police Department to change their policies. As of the 22nd, as many as 600 special restaurants (the general term for cafes, taverns, etc. with female staff) have applied to change to ordinary restaurants. Although students have been prohibited from entering this path, it is clear that merchants have been hit hard in their business. At the same time, it is clear that the red-light districts in Tokyo have always been taken care of by students and have been exposed until now. (Rilian Telegram, 22nd)

England-Australia Air Race

Comet Arrives in Darwin Harbor After Flying Through the Treacherous Timor Sea Section

Venturing Towards the Destination with Damaged Aircraft

Dutch Aircraft Rush to Catch Up from Java

Morrison Couple Withdraw Midway

British Officer Gilman Dies in Crash

(London) On the third day of the England-Australia air race, two things were shocking. One was the withdrawal of the Morrison couple due to aircraft damage, and the other was that the aircraft driven by Scott and Black arrived in Darwin Harbor at 11:08 AM this morning, which can be called magical. Unfortunately, their aircraft "Comet" now needs major repairs. Whether it can complete the entire journey in time and win the championship is now a question. According to Scott's interview with Reuters, one engine was damaged in the Timor Sea, so they only flew for two and a half hours with one engine.

The Dutch aircraft Douglas, which ranked second, arrived in Batavia at 10:36 AM. They landed in Alor Setar in the northwest corner of Malaya seven hours ago and resumed at 4:07 AM.

Flying 400 miles and landing in Singapore at 7:02 AM, they urgently refueled and inspected the aircraft, spending 32 minutes. Then, at 7:34 AM, they resumed flying to Darwin Harbor, 2,084 miles away. Then the weather turned bad and there was wind and rain. (Reuters Telegram, 22nd)

(Darwin Harbor) British aviators Scott and Black arrived here first in the England-Australia long-distance flight competition. One of the two aircraft engines has been damaged. According to Scott, the engine malfunctioned while flying over the Timor Sea, but they still tried to continue moving forward. If repairs are not possible in time, they will try to fly to Melbourne with the power of only one engine. At 1:35 PM (Greenwich time), the two have already flown out and set off for Melbourne. (Havas Telegram, 22nd)

(London) British aviators Scott and Black are one of the fastest groups in the England-Australia long-distance flight competition. The two arrived at Darwin Harbor, Australia, at 12:08 AM (Greenwich time) this morning. From the time they departed from London, the journey took a total of 52 hours, 33 minutes, and 30 seconds, which is 4 days, 13 hours, and 11 minutes less than the record set by Australian aviator Ulm. Assuming they flew in a straight line, their average speed per hour was 281 kilometers. However, the two stopped four times along the way, each time for more than an hour, and the flight did not follow a straight south line, so the actual speed was more than this number. Scott and Black are now flying intermittently towards Melbourne. The next fastest are Dutch aviators Asjes and Geysendorffer. American aviators Turner and Pangborn arrived at Alor Setar on the Malay Peninsula at 10:51 AM (Greenwich time) this morning and are ranked third. (Havas Telegram, 22nd)

Continued telegram: American aviators Turner and Pangborn narrowly escaped an accident when they landed in Baghdad yesterday morning. They departed from Allahabad at 11:45 PM last night and arrived at Alor Setar at 10:45 AM this morning, leaving only four minutes before continuing their journey.

Among the remaining aircraft, the aircraft driven by Wright arrived in Athens today. It flew from Athens to Nicosia at 2:15 AM and continued forward at 9:10 AM. Lieutenant Shaw arrived in Athens at 10:55 AM this morning. Military officers Davis and Hill flew out of Athens at 3:55 AM and arrived in Nicosia three and a half hours later. Australian young aviator Melrose flew out of Nicosia at 6:45 AM this morning. British aviators Jones and Waller were stranded in Karachi due to fog and finally flew out at 4:15 AM this morning, arriving in Allahabad at 8:32 AM. Lieutenant Hansen departed from Alipore last night and arrived in Baghdad at 9:44 AM this morning. Hewitt and Kay flew out of Baghdad at 7:30 AM this morning. McGregor and Walker flew from Bushire to Karachi at 12:30 PM this afternoon. Three other aircraft flew out of Rome in the early hours of today. The aircraft driven by Brookes is still stranded in Bouches, France, due to severe engine damage.

There were originally 20 aircraft participating in the race, but now there are only 13 left. The Morrison couple's aircraft withdrew today, as did two Dutch aircraft, one driven by Asjes and Geysendorffer, and one driven by Bralle and Heimswijk. Another was the aircraft driven by Steinke and Tentler. (Reuters Telegram, 22nd)

(Allahabad) After arriving here safely, the Morrison couple announced that they had withdrawn from the race. One of their engines was severely damaged, and the cylinder head was also burned through. However, the couple still said that if they could find new parts to repair the aircraft, they would still continue moving forward. Before they departed from Karachi last night to come here, they were still full of hope of winning. However, due to getting lost, they landed in Jabalpur, which is 830 miles east of Karachi and 200 miles southwest of Allahabad. However, they finally arrived here at 5:25 AM, 46 hours and 58 minutes after flying out of Mildenhall Aerodrome. (Reuters Telegram, 22nd)

(Rome) British Air Force officer Gilman departed from Rome at 3:55 AM this morning. He crashed and caught fire after flying to Civitavecchia, resulting in his being burned to death. This is the first major misfortune in the England-Australia air race. (Reuters Telegram, 22nd)

(London) In the England-Australia air race, the Comet driven by British aviators Scott and Black is still in the leading position. In less than 40 hours after departure, it has flown approximately 7,063 miles. The progress yesterday was particularly amazing. After leaving Allahabad at 10:15 AM, it arrived safely at the third stop, Singapore, at 10:30 PM, flying 2,210 miles. This was the first sea crossing in the journey. After arriving, they hurriedly refueled and carried supplies. Then, at 11:42 PM, they took off again and headed towards Darwin Harbor, Australia, which is one of the most dangerous sections of the entire journey, measuring 2,084 miles and requiring passage through the shark-infested Timor Sea. When the Comet landed in Singapore last night, it was in danger of capsizing due to a sudden change in wind direction. According to Scott's interview with Reuters, it was very difficult after departing from Allahabad, but the engine was working very well. They could have arrived in Singapore earlier, but they decided to reduce speed to avoid overworking the engine and to land during the day. They now hope to reach Darwin directly without stopping.

The Dutch aircraft Douglas is in second place but is many hours behind the Comet. The pilots Parmentier and Moll still hope to be in the lead. The aircraft flew from Allahabad to Calcutta at 5:40 PM and arrived in Rangoon at 10:15 PM. Late yesterday night, it set off towards Singapore. Before departing from Calcutta, it told Reuters that they planned to land at every major airfield along the way. Although it would take longer, they still hoped to be in the lead. They now believe that Scott and Black are flying at full strength, which means that their engine is overworked. Parmentier said that the flight from Baghdad to Allahabad was very smooth, flying at an altitude of about 12,000 feet. He did not want to overwork the engine, but after Singapore, he planned to go all out. German woman Reitsch, who was on board the aircraft, praised Parmentier and Moll's aviation skills. She also said that they spent four minutes because a passenger landed in Allahabad. (Reuters Telegram, 22nd)

(Paris) According to a message received by "L'Intransigeant" from London, a large aircraft of the British Air Force, carrying inspectors from the Royal Aero Club, crashed while inspecting the times of the pilots participating in the London-Australia flight. The pilot and inspectors, a total of six people, were killed on the spot. (Havas Telegram, 21st)

Liu Zhenhua Returns to Anhui from Beijing

(Nanjing) Anhui Chairman Liu Zhenhua has completed his audience with Wang and reported on Anhui's political affairs. He returned to Anhui by car from the Nanjing-Wuhu Road on the morning of the 22nd. (Special Telegram, 22nd)

(Wuhu) Liu Zhenhua arrived in Wuhu from Beijing on the 22nd and went to Huizhou in the evening. Wuhu rice merchants requested that disaster relief rice be collected at the ocean silver price, but Liu did not agree. (Special Telegram, 22nd)

Measures for the Restoration of the Shanghai-Guangdong Air Route

(Nanjing) The China National Aviation Corporation has completed the construction of a radio station to restore the Shanghai-Guangdong air route. Manager Dai Enji of the company telegraphed the Beijing office, stating that the route will resume flights from November 2nd, flying from Shanghai to Guangdong every Friday at 6:30 AM and from Guangdong to Shanghai every Sunday at 6:30 AM, arriving on the same day, passing through Shanghai, Wenzhou, Fuzhou, Xiamen, and Shantou. At the beginning of the service, it will only transport mail and will not carry passengers for the time being. (Special Telegram, 22nd)

The Government of Hubei Province Requests Increased Subsidies

(Nanjing) The government of Hubei Province has submitted a request for an additional monthly subsidy of 200,000 yuan. The Executive Yuan has instructed the Ministry of Finance to review the request and submit a response. (Dispatch on the 22nd)

Guo Le, Chairman of the United Shanghai Cotton Mills, Petitions the Ministry of Industry

(Nanjing) Guo Le, Chairman of the United Shanghai Chinese Cotton Mills, accompanied by his secretary Zhang Zemin, arrived in Nanjing. On the 22nd, they visited Peng Xuepei and Liu Yinfei at the Ministry of Industry of the Executive Yuan. They stated that the consolidated tax on cotton yarn could not be further increased and requested the government to revise the grading system for the consolidated tax on cotton yarn, changing the current two-tier system to a four-tier system. Liu and Peng promised to forward the request to President Wang and Minister Chen for review and instructions. They are scheduled to meet with President Wang and Minister Kong again on the 23rd to explain the difficulties in detail and present their views on revising the grading system. (Dispatch on the 22nd)

Completion of the Report on External Affairs for the Fifth National Congress

(Nanjing) The report on external affairs for the Fifth National Congress has been completed by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and submitted to the Executive Yuan, which will forward it to the National Government for compilation and submission to the Central Committee for review. The report contains over 50,000 words and covers various diplomatic events from the opening of the Fourth National Congress in November of the 20th year of the Republic to the present. It is divided into twelve main sections: (1) Important diplomatic matters, (2) Conclusion and amendment of treaties, (3) Approval, accession to and withdrawal from international conventions, (4) Participation in treaty matters, (5) Establishment of consulates, (6) Passport and visa matters, and manifest attestation matters, (7) Tax matters, (8) Commercial affairs, (9) Matters relating to the Boxer Indemnity, (10) Concession and jurisdiction matters, (11) Overseas Chinese affairs, (12) International publicity. (Dispatch on the 22nd)

Closing of the Land Administration Society Discussion

(Nanjing) The Chinese Land Administration Society continued its discussion on the implementation regulations of the Land Law on the 22nd, discussing more than 30 proposals regarding the organization of land administration agencies and land rent issues. All the proposals were discussed and resolved, and the meeting has now concluded. (Dispatch on the 22nd)

Progress of the Huai River Diversion Project

(Nanjing) In addition to the 6 million yuan in hydraulic engineering bonds allocated by the Jiangsu Provincial Government for the Huai River diversion project into the sea, a loan of 5 million yuan has been negotiated with the Central Boxer Indemnity Board. Construction will begin on the first day of next month, and each county along the Huai River has been ordered to conscript a total of 160,000 laborers. All necessary tools and equipment will be provided by the laborers themselves. The entire project will be divided into seven sections, each with an engineer in charge. It is preliminarily planned to complete the project by the end of April of next year. (Dispatch on the 22nd)

Jiangsu Province Anti-Smoking Investigation Training Class

(Zhenjiang) The Provincial Anti-Smoking Investigation Training Class held a special nighttime education session on the 22nd to practice and test the students' hearing, listening skills, and directional judgment in preparation for future work. The exercise covered Beigushan, Dongwu Road, Zhongzheng Road, and Dashikou, ending at dawn. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 22nd)

Jiangsu Province Adds Charcoal-Powered Vehicles

(Zhenjiang) The trial use of charcoal-powered vehicles in Jiangsu Province has yielded excellent results. The speed is comparable to that of ordinary gasoline-powered vehicles, and fuel consumption can be reduced by three-quarters. The Highway Administration has decided to add more of these vehicles for use. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 22nd)

Loan for Jiangsu Provincial Bonds to be Signed

(Zhenjiang) The loan for Jiangsu public bonds has been agreed upon, with 8 million yuan mortgaged at 60% of the face value, with an interest rate of 8% and a repayment term of two years. The contract will be signed within the week. The funds will be used for industrial relief in the Jiangnan region and the diversion of the Huai River into the sea. (Dispatch on the 22nd)

Huang Zhongxiang Flies from Hankou Back to Nanjing

(Chongqing) Huang Zhongxiang, the Party Affairs Inspector for the Sichuan-Shaanxi bandit areas, has completed his mission. He flew from Chengdu to Chongqing on the 21st. After attending the memorial week service at the Provincial Special Envoy's Office on the 22nd and giving a report, he is scheduled to fly to Hankou and then back to Nanjing by plane on the 23rd. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 22nd)

Cooperative Management in Various Counties of Hubei Province is Excellent

(Hankou) Ma Boyuan, Director-General of the Hubei Rural Cooperative Committee, previously went to eastern Hubei to inspect the cooperative situation in various counties. Mr. Ma has returned to Hankou a few days ago. According to a Central News Agency reporter, the cooperative management in various counties is excellent. He also stated that the Relief and Famine Prevention Association has agreed to allocate 50,000 yuan to the Committee to sponsor the establishment of preliminary cooperatives, and the funds have been received. Therefore, personnel will be dispatched to various counties within the next few days to start the work. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 22nd)

International Commercial Telegraph

丨Reuter's Special Commercial News on October 22nd丨

Gold and Silver

London Gold Price: The London gold buying price today is 141 shillings and 6 pence, up 3.5 pence.

London Silver Bars: The London silver market is stable, but due to sales from China, prices are lower than on Saturday. The spot price is 23 pence and 8125, down 125. The futures price is 23 pence and 9375, down 0625. India is buying, and speculators are both buying and selling.

Exchange Rates

British-American: The declaration issued after the meeting of the Gold Bloc countries in Brussels on Saturday has made gold coins more attractive in the foreign exchange market this morning, and the US dollar has also risen accordingly. The opening exchange rate for British-American currency was 4 dollars, 9 corners, 5 points, and 625, down 2 points, 125. It gradually fell in the morning, dropping to 4 dollars, 9 corners, 4 points, and 625. By 2 PM, it had rebounded to 4 dollars, 9 corners, 5 points, and 125, down half a point from the opening. Furthermore, one US dollar is equivalent to 4 shillings and 0473 English gold.

British-French: The opening price was 74 francs and 62, 38 pounds lower than on Saturday. After falling another 9 pounds to 74 francs and 53, the price rebounded, rising to 74 francs and 71, 9 pounds higher than the opening.

American-British: In the New York foreign exchange market this morning, the opening exchange rate for American-British currency was 4 dollars, 9 corners, and 5 and a half points, 2 and a half points lower than the closing on Saturday. It later fell to 4 dollars, 9 corners, 5 points, and 25, then slightly recovered to 4 dollars, 9 corners, 5 points, and 625, 125 higher than the opening.

Cotton and Wheat

American Cotton: President Roosevelt's recent speech, which prioritized national lending before handling veterans' benefits, boosted cotton market sentiment. Although the cotton market was slightly hesitant at the opening, prices rose as general sentiment towards commerce improved. The market situation in the morning showed a slight upward trend.

British Cotton: The Liverpool cotton market was more stable this morning. At 1 PM, the January futures price was 6.64, up two pounds.

British Wheat: The Liverpool wheat market was more stable this morning. At 1 PM, the December futures price rose 75 to 5 shillings.

American Wheat: The drought area in the Southwest recently had rain, but it has now stopped. Grain market participants feel more optimistic about grain prices, so wheat opened higher this morning by about half a point compared to Saturday's closing price.

Rubber

London: The rubber market was quiet this morning, but prices were stable. At noon, the transaction price for January-March futures was 6 pence and 9375, the same as on Saturday.

New York: The general sentiment is quite good, as people expect favorable news regarding the authorities' commercial policies. The rubber market has also been affected by this, with prices rising slightly at the opening, and then rising slightly again.

Securities

New York: Factors favorable to the market before the opening of the New York stock market were (1) cheerful sentiment, anticipating exciting developments in Washington, (2) Steel industry reports estimate that steel mills operated at 26.5% of their capacity last week, and that buyers replenished their needs last week without the hesitation and concerns of the past. The unfavorable factor was that merchants still maintain a very cautious attitude, waiting for the clarification of certain uncertain situations. The market was stable at the opening of securities this morning, and prices mostly rose slightly. Merchants generally expect prices to continue to rise slightly, but believe that the upward trend may not last long. Last Day Closing Today Opening 10:40

Xiamen Foreign Exchange Soars After Silver Export Tax

Hong Kong Exchange Rate Up Over 70 Yuan Per Thousand

Some Foreign Exchanges Up Over 200 Yuan

Xiamen Correspondence: Since the Ministry of Finance issued the order to tax silver exports, Xiamen's foreign exchange has soared. For over sixty years, Xiamen has been a port with a trade deficit. In the past five or six years, the trade deficit has reached 20 to 30 million customs taels. Imports are usually eight times greater than exports, with typical annual imports of over 30 million taels while exports are only about 4 million. Initially, remittances from Southeast Asia were about 20 million yuan per year, which largely offset the deficit. Last year, overseas Chinese remittances decreased significantly, leading to a major commercial depression. Foreign exchange and foreign currencies have consistently been at a high peak. This is because the consumption in Xiamen and southern Fujian is mostly of foreign goods, and merchants buy foreign exchange to procure goods. This summer, as silver prices rose, silver and money shops transported large amounts of silver to Hong Kong to purchase British pounds and US dollars to offset foreign exchange. In the three months from July to early October, over 5.6 million yuan worth of silver was exported. At the end of August, the Xiamen Chamber of Commerce once discussed prohibiting silver exports, and the foreign exchange rate immediately rose. Later, the plan was dropped due to opposition from the money shop guild, and the foreign exchange rate was able to return to normal. This time, the Ministry of Finance levied a silver export tax. After the Customs received the telegram from the Fujian Provincial Government, it immediately issued a notice in accordance with the order. However, due to the heavy tax, silver exports naturally disappeared, and the foreign exchange rate soared again. As for the market conditions in recent days, comparing the market conditions on the 13th, which was the day before the tax was levied, with the market conditions on the 18th after the tax was levied (both calculated per thousand yuan), the foreign currency price increases were as follows: Hong Kong currency increased from 1102 yuan to 1800 yuan, an actual increase of 78 yuan; Philippine currency increased from 1370 yuan to 1500 yuan, an actual increase of 130 yuan; Singapore currency increased from 1580 yuan to 1670 yuan, an actual increase of 90 yuan; Annam currency increased from 1780 yuan to 1875 yuan, an actual increase of 95 yuan; Siamese currency increased from 1280 yuan to 1350 yuan, an actual increase of 70 yuan; The Japanese gold ticket, which originally could purchase 1287.5 yuan of Japanese gold per thousand yuan, increased to only purchasing 1120 yuan, an actual increase of 167.5 yuan. The foreign exchange rate, according to the Bank of China's listing, the Hong Kong exchange rate increased from 1101.5 to 1175 yuan (calculated per thousand yuan). The Philippine telegraphic transfer increased from 75.375 to 63.25, the Java telegraphic transfer increased from 54.75 to 48, the Singapore telegraphic transfer increased from 65.625 to 57, and the Rangoon telegraphic transfer increased from 102.125 to 89.5 (the above telegraphic transfers are all calculated by converting 100 yuan of national currency into foreign currency). Furthermore, the US dollar listed by the Central Bank increased from 37 yuan and 50 cents to 33 yuan, 33 cents, and 7.5 (calculated per hundred yuan). It can be seen the impact after the silver export tax was levied. (October 19th)

10,000 Mu of Tobacco Planted in Hui'an, Southern Fujian

Farmers Influenced by Local Scoundrels

County Government Prohibitions Ineffective

Xiamen Correspondence: Fujian Province is an area where opium cultivation is prohibited. The Nanchang Headquarters has issued strict orders to Fujian that anyone who plants opium will be subject to the death penalty. Therefore, various counties are conducting extremely strict inspections. However, the people of Fujian have been misled by the fact that the Fujian Provincial Anti-Smoking Inspection Office has been recruiting merchants to sell special goods, and various counties have been established. They mistakenly believed that special goods could be sold, and tobacco seedlings could also be planted. According to news from Hui'an, it is now the time to plant tobacco seedlings, and people in various parts of Hui'an are planting them in large numbers. The farmers of Hui'an, deceived by the one or two local scoundrels who had previously contracted for tobacco seedling donations, believe the counter-propaganda that special goods can be sold publicly and tobacco seedlings can be planted. Many are stubbornly persisting. The Hui'an County Government confiscated hundreds of buckets of water used by farmers to irrigate tobacco seedlings a few days ago, but it was still ineffective. Investigations show that the following areas within the county have planted tobacco seedlings: Houkeng Township in northern Hui'an has over 300 mu, Fengqi Township has about 200 mu, Thirteen Townships has about 500 mu, Siguxiang Township has about 500 mu, Xudai Township has about 200 mu, Three Townships has over 100 mu, the entire area of Tuling with 53 townships has about 1,000 mu, Nine Townships has over 300 mu, Nanpu Township has over 400 mu, Ciyao has over 200 mu, Lingtou has over 400 mu, Gangxi Nan Village, Kezhai, Panzuo, and E'tou areas have about 700 mu, Batou has 200 mu, Yanyaobei over 100 mu, Eighteen Townships has over 200 mu, Xialupai has 300 mu, Tukeng has over 200 mu, Sanchen has over 500 mu, Shicuo over 100 mu, Linbing has 100 mu, and Tianshefeng has 200 mu. Statistics show nearly 7,000 mu. In addition, in the Zhangkeng, Dawu, and Xingcuo areas of eastern Hui'an, there are also more than 3,000 mu planted, totaling more than 10,000 mu. As for the western part of Hui'an, it is even more self-evident. Historically, Hui'an, Quanzhou, has been a tobacco-producing area, and its people are strong and have always been known as difficult to govern. Therefore, the farmers there disregard the law and openly plant tobacco. (October 19th)

Desperate Autumn Harvest in Jiangxi Province

| Even Drinking Water is a Problem |

Nanchang Correspondence: Since the heavy rain on the seventh day of the fifth lunar month in Jiangxi Province, there has been no continuous heavy rain for five months to date. Although there have been occasional showers in various places in the interim, due to the short duration and uneven distribution, they are merely a drop in the bucket. It is now late autumn, and winter is approaching. Farmers have reached the time for the final reckoning. Statistics for the whole year show that only half of the early rice in high-lying areas survived. The mid-season rice completely dried up, and the late rice was not transplanted at all. In areas near water, although the early rice was not damaged, more than half of the mid-season rice died, and only three or four tenths of the late rice was saved. According to reports from various places, the autumn harvest is completely nonexistent, and dry crops cannot be planted either. Green manure such as flowering plants, which are planted in the autumn, have not been sown at all. The cracked fields are a vast expanse of white, evoking the lament of "no green grass in the fields." No matter where, the lakes, harbors, ponds, and weirs are all dried up. Most of the wells are also dry, except for those with springs. Drinking water is extremely difficult in various places, so the food situation is causing great panic among the people.

Guangzhou Vegetable Merchants Request Abolition of Vegetable Export Tax

Since the Vegetable Tax was Collected

40% of Vegetable Merchants have Gone Bankrupt

Guangzhou Correspondence: Guangdong Province has the most miscellaneous taxes in the country. In addition to national and provincial taxes, there are also municipal taxes. The most notable municipal taxes in Guangzhou are the vegetable export tax and the fruit entry tax. The vegetable export tax is the most painful for farmers and merchants. Since it was first levied in September of the 21st year of the Republic, vegetable merchants have suffered great losses. In recent years, all industries have declined, and goods exports have sharply decreased, but the Guangzhou vegetable export tax is still levied as before, making it even more difficult for vegetable merchants to survive. Therefore, on the 11th of the month, they convened their colleagues to discuss and appeal for the abolition of this miscellaneous tax in order to maintain their livelihoods. It was decided to telegraphically request the higher authorities to quickly abolish the vegetable export tax to relieve the merchants' hardship. The second step is to hold a large-scale petition to achieve their goal, and they plan to draft a telegram requesting the abolition of the tax, which states, "Our vegetable stall merchants and farmers throughout the province have been suffering from the Guangzhou vegetable export tax for three years now. All kinds of abuses, such as the very cumbersome tax reporting procedures, are often penalized for slight errors, often causing the goods to spoil and losing their capital. It is unknown how many people have suffered such losses. Statistics for the past few years show that over 40% of our vegetable stall operators have gone bankrupt, and countless workers have lost their jobs, truly breaking all previous records. On the one hand, they are affected by the economic downturn, and on the other hand, they are oppressed by heavy taxes, inevitably leading to bankruptcy. Our colleagues have already tasted this bitter experience. After much pain, we have no choice but to jointly appeal to the authorities to abolish the Guangzhou vegetable export tax, which harms merchants and farmers, but we have not yet been approved. The decline of our industry is already obvious, but the authorities have not bothered to consider the suffering of our farmers and merchants. In this autumn of global economic recession, how can our Guangdong be an exception? The sluggish commercial situation goes without saying, and our colleagues have also been affected by the decline of the countryside in recent years. If we are further oppressed by heavy taxes, we will inevitably all perish together. Our country's production is backward, and we should be supporting agriculture instead of ruthlessly levying heavy taxes to destroy it. In short, the vegetable export tax is directly enough to sentence our colleagues to death, and indirectly it hinders agricultural production. Our colleagues have no choice but to strongly request the authorities to abolish the tax in order to save the farmers and merchants from danger. We hope that you will maintain it and immediately order the abolition of this vegetable export tax, so that the fish trapped in a dry rut can be revived, and we will be grateful, and agriculture will be fortunate." (14th)

Northwest Inspection Report by our special reporter, Geng Ya

What Was Seen After Departing from Longxi

Since Lanzhou to Suzhou, in recent years there has been a merchant operating automobiles, using the main road to transport passengers and goods. However, most of the goods transported east to Suzhou and west to Pingjin are carried by camels from Mongolia, so the automobile business is particularly sluggish. If traveling by large cart, the price per cart is about three silver dollars per travel day and one dollar per rest day. According to the postal station route, it takes eighteen days to reach Suzhou. If going beyond the pass to Xinjiang, one must change carts in Suzhou. The reporter returned to Lanzhou from Qinghai, just as the Tianjin Huamei Company had five cars coming from Xi'an, planning to continue westward, going beyond the pass to transport sheep intestines. Therefore, I contacted them for a ride and set off on July 15th.

We left Lanzhou North Gate in the morning, passing Zhenyuan Bridge, commonly known as the Yellow River Iron Bridge, which is thirty yards long and twenty-three feet wide. The river water comes from the west and flows eastward, the bridge spanning north and south, a magnificent engineering feat. During the Ming Dynasty, twenty-four boats were used to float rafts to carry vehicles and horses. It was not until the first year of the reign of Emperor Xuantong of the Qing Dynasty that this bridge was rebuilt. Last month, a sedan car coming from Ningxia to Lanzhou was charged a dime for bridge repair when crossing the bridge. Also, when returning from Qinghai through Xiguan here, I was also asked to pay a "jiawozi" donation of five dimes. This time, the automobiles started from South Gate, then Xiguan, then North Gate, then Zhenyuan Bridge, moving majestically. Everywhere we went, people just moved to the sides. I never heard anyone asking for donations. This is simply because the American flag with thirteen stripes and forty-eight stars was fluttering at the head of each car. Suddenly, I remembered that when I went to Qinghai last time, no one checked the inns at any of the stops, which gave me a sense of peace in the villages. When returning, although the scenery was the same, the innkeepers called us "old customers." But at each stop, especially in the area where Gansu and Qinghai meet, a group of military police, seemingly descended from the sky, closely questioned our passports (besides the reporter, there was also a doctor from Qinghai Zhongshan Hospital and a Zhang-surname itinerant photographer from Lanzhou, all of whom were Chinese). They also collected police donations, which could not help but make one sigh, "It's easy to go, but hard to return." Now that American cars (of the five drivers, four were with high noses and blue eyes) drive into our heartland as if entering a no-man's land, it dawned on me that the ease of going to Qinghai was indeed due to the protection of the British and American tobacco company employees, Mr. Ba and Mr. Di.

After crossing the bridge and traveling west for about a mile, we exited Jincheng Pass. Along the north bank of the Yellow River, date forests stretched as far as the eye could see, and the waves of wheat were lovely. After ten or so miles, we turned into the northwest mountain gorge. From then on, we no longer saw the Yellow River. The road traveled through sandy pits, winding and flat. If it rained, we should beware of mountain floods. The peaks on both sides were rugged and bare, without a single tree. In the middle, there was a mountain that looked like a Western-style building, with the bank collapsed like a wall and grass covering it like a roof, which was quite interesting. Ten miles away was Zhujiajing, with forty households. They farmed on flat sandy land, growing melons, wheat, and poppies. There was a small school in the temple, teaching both the Four Books and science. Thirty miles away, we climbed up a slope, then zigzagged down slowly, and arrived at Yujiawan, with about thirty households. Nearby two or three postal stations lacked water sources. Residents dug deep cellars, with small openings and large bellies, and lined their surroundings with oiled mud without any gaps. When it rained heavily and mountain floods broke out, they raced to put the water into the cellars to use as drinking water, which they called "cellar water." The cellars for storing water did not interfere with each other. Families with large populations even had to dig several cellars in the fields. Each time after drawing water, they had to seal the opening. Travelers watering their horses had to pay ten copper coins per head. The water was yellow and unclean, and even the horses were reluctant to drink much. If wells were dug to find springs, they had to be dug more than two hundred yards deep, but the spring water obtained still tasted bitter and salty, and was inferior to the taste of the cellar water. If there was a prolonged drought without rain, not only would the crops fail, but people would also die of thirst. Elsewhere, eating depends on heaven, but here even drinking water depends on heaven, so the people's level of superstition is even higher than elsewhere.

Traveling west from Yujiawan for twenty miles, we reached Hajiazui, with over a hundred households. Forty percent of them were farmers, and sixty percent were salt miners. About a mile outside the village, the ground was covered with salt. It appeared after the rain, and could be obtained by digging and sweeping. Every hundred pounds were sold for thirty cents, but the salt tax was as high as two dollars and seventy cents. The annual tax could reach forty to fifty thousand dollars. Twenty miles away was Alkali River Shop, where people used dung bricks as fuel. Thirty miles away was Xujia Inn, with several water mills, also known as Xujia Mill. The soil was fertile, the forests were lush, and the clear springs flowed continuously, which was refreshing. Five miles away was Red Castle, a bustling market town in Yongdeng (Pingfan). There were guards at both the east and west gates. Ten miles away was Zhengjiadun, another ten miles was Qingbao Fortress, twenty miles was South Datong Post, thirty miles was Pingfan Old City, also known as Manchu City, and five miles was Yongdeng County. We stayed at the South Gate. That day, we traveled a total of two hundred and ten miles.

The city was built of bricks, over ten yards high. The next morning, I went into the city for a tour. The streets in the center were low and concave, and after the rain, they were filled with sewage. The residents' houses and courtyards were large and spacious, but all were old and dilapidated, with not a single new building. Under the eaves of the streets, male and female beggars lay huddled together, smoking. An atmosphere of age-old decline permeated the entire city. After leaving the city and returning to the inn, it was only nine o'clock in the morning, but the so-called newly arrived "flower girls" were already leaning against the doors of various inns, selling their smiles. Starting so early, one can imagine that there were no guests to entertain at night. According to the innkeeper, "The farmers and merchants living outside the city are busy all day long, still worried about having no clothes or food. How would they dare to seek pleasure with prostitutes? The civil and military officials living in the city, because the city gates are closed at night, are unable to go out and play. And there is an official decree that the flower girls are not allowed to enter the city to solicit customers, so their business is very bleak. It is very pitiful to look at them." From this, it is not difficult to see what Yongdeng's market is like. When ascending to a high place for a distant view, there was a green field with tall trees, flowers in full bloom, and abundant beans and wheat. The ancient saying "fertile land west of the river" was truly worthy of the name. However, it ultimately could not remedy the depression of the market and the bankruptcy of the rural areas. Is it not because the taxes are heavy and the "land" is of no benefit to the people?

After breakfast, we traveled in the rain, passing through a deep ditch five or six miles long and only six or seven feet wide, with slippery mud walls, where the car got stuck several times. It was commonly called "seventy-two trails where your feet don't stay dry," which shows how difficult it was to travel by car. After the ditch, we climbed up to a bank road, where there was a village called Machanggou, ten miles from the city. The village women came out to watch when they heard the sound, all covering their mouths and noses, as if quite shy. Then we reached the Zhenqiang River, where the drizzle was incessant and the wheels were rattling, giving one the warning that "it is impossible to proceed." There was a wooden bridge, said to be "Wusheng Pass," with plaques at both ends, one saying "Road Leading to Xinjiang and Longxi" and the other saying "Peaceful Waves in Nine Channels." Crossing to the left bank, we could vaguely see a village hidden in the green willow trees, which was Wusheng Post. A rider came towards us, speeding past in the rain, looking hurried and attracting attention. After traveling about seven or eight miles, we saw a woman in her forties, completely soaked, panting and dragging a cane as she ran. But because she yielded to the side of the road for the car, she sat down in the mud and could not get up. The car also stopped at the postal station, as the road was slippery and difficult to travel. That day we only traveled forty miles. Amid the many discussions of the crowd, we learned that the rider who had passed by hastily was a tax collector, because he had come here three times to collect taxes, but the headman had no money to pay. The tax collector angrily whipped the headman, who fainted and fell to the ground. Therefore, he fled quickly, and the woman chasing after him was the headman's wife.

The Riot of Farmers in Suzhou Is Pacified

In Xietang Chefang, Weiting Waikuatang, and the suburbs of Loufengmen in Suzhou, farmers were dissatisfied with the wasteland reclamation and gathered to riot. From the 19th night to the 22nd, it was investigated that a total of 26 houses of tax collectors, etc., were demolished and burned, totaling 205 rooms, as well as more than 10 boats, 7 or 8 farm boats, and 400 to 500 piculs of rice. On the 21st night at 9:30, farmers from Xuanzhu Village and Beiwangdun Village on the edge of Yangcheng Lake, etc., also beat gongs to gather more than 100 people, from Weiting south to Fangjing Village, five miles east of Waikuatang along the Jinghu Road, preparing to beat up the house of tax collector Chen Shaolin. Fortunately, the farmers in this village refused to join and pleaded for Chen's exemption. This riot of farmers then changed direction to the northeast and arrived at the house of tax collector Cha Fengkui in Lujing Village, preparing to set it on fire. However, Cha Fengkui had always been enthusiastic about public welfare matters in the countryside and often made donations. The farmers in the nearby villages had automatically gathered at Cha's house from the 20th night to protect it. Cha also slaughtered two pigs and set up a wine feast to entertain them. When the rioting farmers rushed into the village, Cha's house was full of people eating and drinking heartily. Upon hearing the news, they each carried farm tools and went out to meet the enemy. Thus, a major melee broke out between the two sides. As a result, the rioting farmers were defeated and two people were injured. They were arrested and sent to the Weiting Police Station. Meanwhile, the county government secretly ordered the Public Security Bureau to arrest Lu Genshou, Shi Jinhu, Shi Shuangbao, Zhang Sifa, Zhang Jinlong, Wang Abing, Chen Genshou, and seven others in Waikuatang on the 21st night to the 22nd morning. Shi, as a village elder, confessed that on the 19th night at 7 or 8 o'clock, many people held a meeting at his house to discuss burning the tax collector's house. The remaining confessions were all forced to agree. On the 22nd, there were no accidents in the Chexie and other areas, and the riot was expected to be pacified. The provincial government had sent the first battalion and one company of the provincial security team, with 200 soldiers, to Suzhou on the afternoon of the 22nd to be stationed outside Loufengmen to deter the county government. The county government also found out that during this riot, the farmers in Chexie, Weikua, and other villages, in addition to using farm tools as weapons and beating gongs, also had police whistles. First, the A village sounded the police whistle to gather people, and then set off with gongs. When they reached B village, they handed the police whistle over to B village, and C village and D village passed it on in turn, called "snake molting," so the rioting area spread very widely.

The Shanghai Chinese Track and Field Team and the Suzhou Healthy and Beautiful Track and Field Team held an anti-sporting movement in Suzhou on the 21st. Blood was flowing at the time, and he was sent to the hospital for treatment. Because the injury was quite serious, his life was in danger.

Second Batch of Opium from Wuxi Transported to Xi for Sale

Since its opening, the three local opium shops of Yongxing, etc., have been very successful. The first batch of 5,000 taels of official opium was sold out in less than two days. Bandits Rob Ship and Shoot Crew

The ships on the Xueyanqiao waterway at the junction of Xi and Wu, traveling between Xi and Yi, often encounter bandit ships. Therefore, they agreed with the three ships of Luquqiao, Zhouqiao, and Panjiaqiao to meet in Zhangjin Town at about 5:00 pm every day and set off together. The day before yesterday evening, the four ships set off as usual, with the Xueyanqiao ship sailing in the lead. When they reached near Chendiangang at Yabaqiao, Shatangying, they suddenly encountered a bandit ship with nine bandits on board, with a six-inch Browning pistol. They went on board to rob. The Zhouqiao ship's crew Chen Genshou and Chen Ashou, two brothers, fought with the bandits. As a result, Ashou was shot in the waist, and Genshou was thrown off the bridge onto the shore by the bandits, suffering serious injuries. Chen Erxiao, a passenger on the Panjiaqiao ship, was strong and powerful, and also fought fiercely with the bandits. Due to being outnumbered, he was beaten and injured by the bandits. At that time, gongs were sounded loudly, and the villagers in the area all held farm tools to capture the bandits. They intercepted a bandit ship and caught _ bandits. The rest escaped. They were sent to the Zhangshe Public Security Bureau and transferred to the Public Security Bureau for investigation. The injured Chen Ashou and Chen Genshou _ people were sent to the Brothers Hospital for treatment. Ashou's life was in danger, but Genshou was not in serious condition.

Robbery and Arson by Bandits in the Fourth District of Changzhou

Tan Shengda's family in Huangjiatang, Chengshu Township, Fourth District of Wu Yi, was robbed by more than ten bandits on the night of the 18th of this month. Each held a pistol and flashlight, etc., and climbed over the wall to enter, wantonly searching and robbing, and arrested Tan Shengda, the victim, forcing him to hand over silver and property. When Tan refused to comply, they poured kerosene on his body and set it on fire, causing serious injuries to his waist and other places. After searching for about half an hour, they fled with the stolen goods. After the incident, Tan was swollen with injuries all over his body and died on the 20th. His son, Canhai, immediately rushed to report to the Fourth District Office to request the arrest of the thieves and the return of the stolen goods. The district chief Chen Yi reported to the county court on the 21st to request an autopsy. Personnel were dispatched to the countryside today (the 22nd) for an autopsy to facilitate the arrest.
