Weather Report

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated: Shandong is sunny and cloudy, with winds from the southwest to the northwest. The middle and lower reaches of the Yangtze River have winds from the northeast to the southeast and are windless, with fog in the morning. The East China Sea is cloudy and rainy, with northeast winds. The hurricane near the Xisha Islands is still moving to the west-northwest. There is a low-pressure area in western China. The center of the hurricane at 6:00 AM was within 60 miles of 16 degrees north latitude and 114 degrees east longitude, moving westward. The wind force is strong. In addition, in the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday, the highest temperature in Shanghai was 78.4 degrees and the lowest was 55.0 degrees. On the same day last year, the highest temperature was 73.6 degrees and the lowest was 57.7 degrees.

Ziyuehua Discusses Impressions of Traveling in Europe

The World War is Undeniable

Foreigners Praise Credit Investigation Work

Mr. Ziyuehua, Manager of the Shanghai Commercial & Savings Bank, was sent abroad last autumn by the bank to investigate banking businesses in various countries. Colleagues at the China Credit Association, because Mr. Zi is one of the directors of the association and the standing director of the China Credit Bureau established by the association, entrusted him to investigate the status of credit bureaus in various countries to learn from them. Mr. Zi returned to China last month, and colleagues from the association specially welcomed him at the Bank Club the other day and invited Mr. Zi to report on his investigation. The reporter from the Shen Shi News has recorded the details as follows:

Each Country Has Three Abundances According to Mr. Zi, this trip was extremely thought-provoking. Seeing the increasing decline of overseas Chinese, the incompetence of diplomats, and the contempt for people of color, everything is enough to make people weep. Some government officials and celebrities often go abroad under the guise of inspection, but in fact, they do nothing and waste national funds. In this year's Chicago World's Fair, each pavilion was splendid and magnificent, extremely attentive to display, but the Chinese pavilion was simple and crude, like a small stall in the market. Beside it were the Japanese and Manchurian pavilions, and comparing the two, one felt ashamed. After the war, the industry and commerce of various countries have made rapid progress, and all measures are based on rationalization as the standard. Entering such an environment, one can only sigh with admiration. However, the social structure of each advanced industrial and commercial country has its own contradictions. Nowadays, democratic countries all have three abundances: many beggars, many prostitutes, and many airplanes and cannons. The inevitability of a second world war is undeniable, but once the war breaks out, the transformation of the economic system will be difficult to describe.

The American Banking System Mr. Zi continued, although the American banking industry is very developed, its system is not good. The laws of each state are different. Except for major policies such as military affairs and diplomacy, which are controlled by the federal government, other things are handled separately. There are more than fifty kinds of banking laws promulgated throughout the country. With so many differences, the malpractices are naturally great. Moreover, the American population is complex, and their ancestors were immigrants from various countries, so their thinking is also very inconsistent, which has a great impact on the laws and regulations. On the contrary, the British system is relatively sound. Since there has been a bank, it has had a history of 150 years, experienced many twists and turns, and gradually improved to this day. American banks mostly arose after the European war with the expansion of industry and commerce. The organization is not precise, and once a panic occurs, a crisis arises. Our country's banking system has not yet been established. What to do in the future should be carefully selected.

British and American Credit Investigation Business Yu (Mr. Zi refers to himself) was entrusted by you when he went abroad to investigate the credit investigation business in various countries. Although my talent is limited, I dare not neglect my work. I am a director of the the Credit Association. Whenever there is an opportunity, I will visit. The credit investigation offices in their country are also jointly organized by various entrepreneurs, which is similar to the establishment of a credit investigation office in China by our association. Representatives of various entrepreneurs often gather at a certain time and place to exchange news and study safe methods of lending. The American credit investigation offices are the most developed in the world: (1) Because the American banking system is imperfect and uncoordinated, although each bank has a special department for investigation, it still has to seek help from the credit investigation office. (2) The credit investigation office has a good organization and handles affairs quickly. Because its service scope covers all walks of life, it not only helps banks but also benefits other industrial and commercial circles. The scope of individual cases is large, and there are more than 1,000 office workers. The organization and scope of the British credit investigation office are inferior to those of the United States. The buildings are generally not very clean, and the business is not eager to make progress. This is due to the traditional conservative habits of the British.

China's Credit Investigation Business I once visited the India Eastern Credit Bureau (Indian Eastern Association) in the United Kingdom (Note: This is the British special agent of the China Credit Bureau, and the China Credit Bureau is also the agent of the credit bureau in China.) I was shown a report sent by the China Credit Bureau by the manager of the bureau. He said that the China Credit Bureau, which was only established for two years, was able to make such a detailed report, which was very strange. However, some reports have too much material, which makes it difficult for readers to understand at a glance, so it is best to make a brief introduction at the beginning of the article. This is especially good. This can be used as a model for this office.

Impressions of the Credit Investigation Office On the third day after I returned to China, I came to this office. After being away for a year, the archive materials have increased a lot. Various systems have been improved, and the business is expanding day by day. The office staff are busy with work, and no one is idle. The atmosphere of vitality is revealed everywhere, and I feel inexplicably happy. However, all of this is due to the efforts of the directors and representatives. Although I have the name of a director, I am ashamed of not having contributed and feel deeply guilty.

Page 13

Free Talk

European Satirists

— Wei Ming

Great satirists are mostly "full of untimely things." If you add a little persecution or experience of wandering, then his satire will be particularly sharp and insightful, even if the times are different, it is still thought-provoking.

Swift's "Gulliver's Travels" is still a favorite of children and "big children" to this day. I am afraid that it is not only because of the beauty of the words and the lightness of the imagination, nor is it simply because it satirizes the England of the time, but rather because it is "the long journey of the human soul," like Goethe's "Faust" and Cervantes' "Don Quixote." And Swift's life "like a poisoned rat angrily dying in a hole" (to use his own words) was a prerequisite for him to be able to sharply depict "the long journey of the human soul."

If Cervantes had not been kidnapped by pirates and enslaved for five years, if the wife he married at the age of thirty-seven had been rich, if he had not been forced to go to jail every day after his marriage due to debt (part of his "Don Quixote" was probably written in prison), then, whether "Don Quixote" could have far surpassed the scripts he wrote in his early years may be a question? Now we all know "Don Quixote," but we don't talk much about the scripts he wrote in his early years.

Dante, who wrote "The Divine Comedy," although he was also an exile, his whole life was much more comfortable than Swift and Cervantes; comfort is also bland. Comfort also made Dante have no other broad world view or outlook on life except to put his political enemies in hell. And how narrow his religious views are!

I like "Faust" more than "The Divine Comedy," but I think that "Faust" and "The Divine Comedy" combined are not as good as "Gulliver's Travels" or "Don Quixote"!

I don't think much of satirists who live comfortably and especially get along well with the society of the time. Such a satirist, following the tastes of the "citizens" of his time, added satire to the "rebellious thinkers," which probably won a lot of applause at the time, but when we read his works now, we only feel bad and feel that he is a clown, and his satire has become his own ugly mask.

One such satirist is Aristophanes, a comedian of ancient Greece.

He was conservative, and he wrote the comedies "The Clouds" and "The Frogs" to mock Socrates and Euripides. He worked hard to mock this philosopher and tragedian because they mercilessly exposed the corruption and ignorance of Athenian society. They attacked traditional ideas.

Aristophanes could not have a broad world view; he was worried about the "civil war" between Athens and Sparta, but the "method of ending the war" he proposed in the comedy "Lysistrata" seems like a clown's joke to us now.

What is his cheap method? It is that the women of Athens and Sparta organized a "sex strike alliance" to subdue the war-loving men. He taught them to: first use their appearance to seduce those men, and when they are impatient, put forward conditions: peace and truce. His method was certainly effective on the "stage."

I remember some time ago, the newspaper said that some pacifist women in Europe and the United States advocated organizing a group to stand in the middle of the battle lines of the warring armies if a world war broke out. Haha, I didn't expect Aristophanes to still have comrades! However, such a "joke" is to divert the world's attention from the truly effective methods of eliminating imperialist war!

Superficial

— Liu Shi

People who don't usually talk about women suddenly hear that he is in love, which arouses a temporary uproar among acquaintances. This is a kind of curiosity and is not surprising. For example, in recent months, I have occasionally moved my pen, and I was actually honored to be mentioned by a certain professor at a certain banquet in Peiping. According to a friend who wrote to me, the professor said that he was very dissatisfied with what I wrote in certain publications, because "a person who reads as much as he does should not write such superficial things. Why doesn't he write something more formal?"

When I received the professor's words, I naturally felt very honored, and at the same time, my jacket was soaked with sweat. I remembered that ten years ago, when the professor was as superficial as this superficial thing, cooking beef in an apartment in Peiping, who would have thought that in just ten years, the distance between us would be so great! The professor is now an authority in the cultural world. Although I have never had the honor to read his "profound" works, I am now living on the sea, relying on writing superficial things to support a lonely little life. Naturally, I am ashamed to death.

I don't feel offended or ashamed when the word "superficial" is used to criticize what I write. Because my original intention in writing was not to be "profound." Although I also flip through books after eating, I have never been abroad or studied with famous teachers. I don't have anything in my stomach, so naturally I can't spout high theories. I'm not ashamed of this. Secondly, the publications that accept my articles are not annual publications of any university, but things for so-called superficial people to read. The editors repeatedly urged me to write in a popular way, otherwise it would affect their sales and everyone would have nothing to eat. Therefore, when I write articles, I always deliberately seek to be superficial and clear in terms of both the form and content of the text, and I don't advocate elegance. I never thought that this kind of publication and my kind of article would be read by high-level people like professors. Therefore, the word superficial is not an insult to me. If it is too elegant, there is a worry about breaking my own and other people's rice bowls.

Thirdly, there is the explanation of the word superficial. I don't know which aspect of my articles the professor's criticism refers to. My "scientific essays," some short articles about reading, I don't admit that their content is childish, ridiculous, or superficial. They do not violate scientific truths, nor have they ever had common sense errors. I adhere to the attitude that a scientist should have. As for the way of expression, I only feel that it is too unpopular, too superficial, and too foreign-style. As for saying that if you have knowledge, you should speak in a way that no one understands. Even if this is true, I have no reason to accept it before I become a university professor.

Finally, I have to state that Shi has not been "reading so much" since leaving Peiping. This is because I am busy with food and clothing, which makes me lazier day by day. But at the same time, I am also looking down on books day by day. I think that if I also sit in some academic institution one day, specializing in selling books, and never see ordinary people other than Western suits all year round, it would be better to hang out in the streets while secretly reading a few broken newspapers under the shade of trees, and borrow one or two books from the circulating library to read, and say a few superficial words. Isn't that more interesting than sitting on the podium and giving a monologue that no one understands?

"Mao Savage"

— TK

Farewell (Continued)

— Cao Ming

Suddenly, a rapid moan was emitted from the deity hall, like the kind of urgent, wailing sound that happens when the silk factory's whistle is about to end, which made the aunt have to leave her beloved baby and go back to the deity hall.

"Gaolao Yao, what do you feel?" The voice started very high, but later gradually became hoarse, "Let's just let it go! You suffering thing." She had already walked to the bedside, and the lamplight was stopped on the uncle's face, which had completely turned dirt yellow.

"Alas, you've buried your life in endurance! Submission is your best way to resolve things. You are even weaker than a little rabbit," she kept shaking her head. "You say that I scold you, I completely disregard you, but I am not a pig or a snot worm, so how can I keep silent and let you be coaxed and bullied by others? But, in fact, you have suffered enough and been completely fooled by others. Where have you ever accepted my advice and encouragement? You are just naked, kneeling before power and tyranny! Gaolao Yao, to this day, I feel that you have not done a single right thing in your life. Just the fact that you were deprived of your own well-cultivated twenty mu of mulberry land is enough to make me hate you to the bone. Think about it, is it a happy thing for a girl who is not yet fifteen years old to marry a husband who is thirty years old and half her height? I won't mention this either. I can only complain about my parents and my horoscope. Which daughter would have such good fortune to choose her husband herself? 丨丨" She crossed one of her legs and placed it on the bed, as if preparing to settle an old debt with her deaf and dumb uncle for a longer time.

"In the past, the mulberry trees that the two of us worked so hard to plant, the silkworms that we raised, and the silk that I worked day and night to make, you lightly, were frightened by the silk merchants and cocoon customers, and you quickly got rid of them; for example, we used our own painstaking efforts to exchange for two cents, but they could exchange for four cents without any effort. You say that small capital eats small, and large capital eats large, and without doing this, you won't even be able to sell a penny—alas, when people chase you, you hide and avoid, can't you bite back?

"Gaolao Yao, can you tell me? Why do you seem so afraid and timid in front of Yao Nan? It is clear that he set a trap to frame you, causing you to suffer a wrongful lawsuit, and secretly gave you forty yuan, and that twenty mu of land has been in his hands for thirty years. I know that you are not greedy for those forty yuan, but why don't you use reason to beat your enemy to death? Do you completely believe that there is no justice in the world anymore?

"In the past thirty years, the world has completely changed. Now, even children know that the Western devils can make silk themselves, and there is so much that they can't use it all, and no one wants ours anymore. Now who is happy to get back a piece of wasteland? It's your own fault that a seventy-year-old is still rolling around in the fields. Since you are willing to suffer dozens of losses, why are you unwilling to admit this one mistake to me? …" She propped her cheek with her hand, staring at the dying patient as if forcing a prisoner to confess.

"Gaolao Yao, I know that you are most afraid of two things in your life, scolding and threats can take your life. A Yao, take advantage of the time when you still have a breath, admit your mistakes, I can still have time to forgive you, so that we can have a better time when we meet underground in the future. Nod your head, … you fool, did you hear my words?" The two of them looked at each other, silent, and what was left was still the painful moaning and the whispers of the silkworms next door.

Later, she turned her face to me and said, "He doesn't understand anything now. In fact, I don't feel anything if he dies, but he asked me several times and I didn't properly burn a bowl of pork porridge and sugar tea for him to eat, and he won't be able to close his eyes when he dies …"

She was silent for a while and then stood up, opened the uncle's bedding, and ordered me, "Go to the rosewood box and take out the shroud. He left a trace of breath waiting for those things. I'll help him change his clothes, so that the rusty machine can walk more comfortably."

The aunt carefully helped the uncle put on his clothes, gently picked him up, so that his soles were placed flat outwards, and comforted him in a kind and comforting tone like coaxing a child:

"Shao Yao, go well on your way, and you don't need to worry about anything. As for me, alas, needless to say, I will definitely live my life as usual. I will also scold people, until my throat is useless, … old ghost!"

While I was sobbing on my aunt's lap, I seemed to hear a small sound like a chicken burping. So I cried out loudly and happily. After a long time, my aunt said to me gently and softly in a businesslike tone:

"Okay, it's almost dawn. Now you run back and tell Brother Ren and Fourth Uncle, and I'll call the undertaker."

I walked out of the door, and the cold wind wrapped around my head. I suddenly felt a few drops of water dripping from my hairline into my neck.

Little West Boy (4)

— Written by Langston Hughes, Translated by Fo Lang

Things are really busy tonight. Some people want to shine their shoes at the same time. They sit on the armrests of the chairs in the reception room. Cindy takes his black shoe box for them to put one foot on while shining. A tall farmer gave him half a dime and gently patted him on the head.

"Really a smart kid," he said to the tea room head.

At about ten o'clock, Miss Maria McCarron's room rang, but Charlie had other things to do. Jew Willis called Cindy to go up and see what she wanted. Miss McCarron had just run in from the snow and with a bulky and ugly man. They were both drunk. Cindy knocked lightly on her door.

"Come in," the man roared.

Cindy opened the door and saw Miss McCarron standing naked in the middle of the floor combing her hair. He stopped at the threshold.

"Hey, come in," the man said. "She won't bite you! Where is that tea room boy? We want some liquor! … Go down and tell Charlie to come up here! He knows what I need!"

Cindy walked away trembling. When he found Charlie, he told him about Miss McCarron. The child was very horrified, because he often heard children of color fascinated to look at white women 丨丨 But this little tea room boy just laughed.

"You're really a dumb little ghost!" he said. "But you've only been here for a while, and you'll see more than that in the future!" He winked and gently touched Cindy with his elbow. "Kid, I've sold ten bottles of liquor tonight!" he whispered happily. "Some are my own!"

Cindy went back to the reception room to shine shoes. A big red-necked guest smoking and a group of merchants drinking in a corner of the room beckoned to him. "Hey, kid! Come here and shine my shoes!" So he took his shoe box from the side and walked to the middle of this group of people, bent his knees in front of this big man, took out his shoe polish can and rag, and went to work.

This white man told embarrassing stories, more obscene than what Cindy had heard in the black barbershop, and not very interesting 丨 some simply made him uncomfortable.

The big man who was having his shoes shined said: "Now I want to talk about one." He said in a southern drawl and a soft blurred tone like some old black people's endings. "This is about a black carbon head going to see Aunt Henny …"

A burst of rude laughter welcomed his beginning of the narration. He was encouraged to talk about others.

"The old black ghost pressed a girl on the bank …" he began to say.

Cindy shined his shoes, put the cloth in the wooden box, stood up and waited for his reward, but the speaker did not pay attention to this black child. Until he finished his story and everyone else laughed heartily, then he looked at Cindy and suddenly grinned.

Education News

British Gengkuan Committee Offers Prizes for Elementary School Textbooks

(Central News Agency, Nanjing, 22nd) The Central Gengkuan Committee has set up three kinds of prizes to encourage publications, with each prize amounting to 4,000 yuan. It seeks public education readers, elementary school songs, and senior elementary school history textbooks. Applicants must send their submissions to the committee before the end of June next year. The announcement date is set for October 1st.

National Academic Work Consultation Office Starts Registration

(Nanjing, 22nd) The National Academic Consultation Office started registering unemployed academic personnel on the 22nd. Forty people went to register and receive registration forms in person, including one woman. More than thirty people applied for registration by mail. After registration reaches a considerable time, a meeting will be held to review the qualifications of registered personnel and then introduce jobs.

The Ministry of Education instructed the Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau that the eighth volume of the elementary school Chinese textbook revised by the World Book Bureau, Lesson 12, is approved for record. In addition, the National English Reader compiled by Lu Dianyang should be approved for review after revision. Recent News from the Zhejiang Hangzhou Normal School Elementary School Education Correspondence Class

The elementary school education correspondence class attached to the Zhejiang Provincial Hangzhou Normal School has been held for three sessions since its establishment, and the results are remarkable. This period is the fourth session. Since the start of registration, elementary school teachers from all over the world have sent letters asking to join, which is very enthusiastic. It is reported that as of yesterday, in addition to the original students, more than 700 new members have joined. The registration period was originally scheduled to end on October 15th, but because students from remote areas repeatedly sent letters saying that due to inconvenient transportation or delayed news, they could not register as scheduled and asked to be allowed to enroll. The school, considering the eagerness of the members to improve their studies, could not let them miss the opportunity, so it approved an extension of one month. Anyone who is interested in joining can go to register. The school has also scheduled to send the first lecture notes on October 25th for the convenience of those who register as scheduled to study as early as possible. It is said that there are a total of nine kinds of lecture notes in this semester, which have been scheduled by the school's extension education office to be distributed in batches on a regular basis.

Jiangsu Elementary Education Facilities (1) by Zhou Fo Hai

Zhou Fo Hai, Director of the Jiangsu Education Department, reported the following at the Provincial Government Memorial Weekly on the 22nd:

Today, I will briefly report on the past facilities and future plans for elementary education in our province.

First, I will explain the development of elementary education in Jiangsu Province over the past three years in terms of numbers. Due to the overall economic decline and financial difficulties, there has not been a significant increase in education funding. Consequently, there has not been substantial development in the quantity of educational undertakings. However, a comparison between the statistics for the 21st year and the 19th year shows some increase in elementary education. In terms of the number of classes, there were 158 provincial school classes in the 19th year and 208 in the 21st year, an increase of 50 classes. The number of county school classes was 11,596 in the 19th year and 14,763 in the 21st year, an increase of 3,167 classes. The number of private school classes was 1,102 in the 19th year and 1,424 in the 21st year, an increase of 322 classes. If we add up the total number of classes in provincial, county, and private schools, the total number of classes in the 19th year was 12,856 and in the 21st year it was 16,395, an overall increase of 3,539 classes. In terms of the number of students, there were 6,537 provincial school students in the 19th year and 8,909 in the 21st year, an increase of 2,372 students, representing an increase of over 36 percent. The number of county school students was 636,711 in the 19th year and 672,563 in the 21st year, an increase of 35,852 students, representing an increase of over 5 percent. The number of private school students was 48,717 in the 19th year and 62,932 in the 21st year, an increase of 14,215 students, representing an increase of over 29 percent. If we add up the total number of students in provincial, county, and private schools, the total number of students in the 19th year was 691,965 and in the 21st year it was 744,404, an overall increase of 52,439 students. The total increase in the number of people compared between these two years, calculated as a percentage, is actually over 7 percent. In terms of funding, the provincial elementary school funding was 289,223 yuan in the 19th year and 337,997 yuan in the 21st year, an increase of 48,774 yuan, representing an increase of over 16 percent. The county elementary school funding was 5,369,379 yuan in the 19th year and 5,511,743 yuan in the 21st year, an increase of 142,364 yuan, representing an increase of over 2 percent. The private elementary school funding was 524,251 yuan in the 19th year and 710,539 yuan in the 21st year, an increase of 186,288 yuan, representing an increase of over 35 percent. If we add up the total funding for provincial, county, and private schools, the total elementary school funding in the 19th year was 6,182,853 yuan and in the 21st year it was 6,560,279 yuan, an overall increase of 377,426 yuan. The total increase in silver dollars compared between these two years, calculated as a percentage, is actually over 6 percent. Looking at all the above increase rates, the increase in students is greatest in provincial schools, followed by private schools. The increase in funding is greatest in private schools, followed by provincial schools. From this, it can be seen that Jiangsu's elementary school education, when compared in terms of numbers, is continuing to progress, but the rate of progress is very slow. If it continues like this, who knows how many years it will take to achieve universal compulsory education? However, the people's burden cannot be increased further, and there is no source of revenue for local education funds. It is difficult to make something out of nothing, even for a skilled housewife.

Now, let's divide the larger projects that have been done in the past and those that are planned for the future into provincial and county-level undertakings, and report them layer by layer.

(1) Past Facilities

(A) Provincially Managed

(1) Establishment of Compulsory Education Experimental Zones. The popularization of compulsory education is important, but how can it be popularized? Many methods have been proposed from various aspects, such as simplified elementary schools, short-term elementary schools, and two-part systems. However, it is difficult to determine which method is the simplest, easiest to implement, and most effective, and it needs to be experimented with. For this reason, in the 22nd year, we established five provincial compulsory education experimental zones. Their task is to comprehensively include all methods of popularizing compulsory education, experiment with them, and observe the results. The locations of the five compulsory education zones are Zhenjiang, Huaiyin, Donghai, Huangdu, and Qixia Mountain. They are all entrusted to the principals of provincial normal schools or rural normal schools for management. The reason for choosing these five locations is that first, Zhenjiang is the capital of Jiangsu Province, but there are very few elementary schools and many school-age children are out of school, so it is necessary to seek relief first, and it can also be established as a model for the entire province. Huaiyin and Donghai are located in northern Jiangsu and are relatively underdeveloped in education. The province should use its strength to subsidize the development of their elementary education. Huangdu and Qixia Mountain are because the results of the rural normal schools in these two places are very good, and the two principals are also very willing to work hard, so they are specially asked to take on this major task in the hope of making new contributions for everyone's reference. As for the teachers in the schools in each compulsory education zone, most of them are using normal school students in the highest grades. On the one hand, it can save public funds, and on the other hand, it can increase the practical experience of normal school students. According to current statistics, there are a total of 49 elementary schools of various natures established in the five compulsory education zones, with 83 classes. (To be continued)

Shanghai Education Association Second Representative Congress

Director Pan Attends the Meeting on Behalf of Mayor Wu to Deliver Instructions

Huang Zao Xiong, Du Gang, and Others Elected as Directors and Supervisors

The Meeting Adjourns at 5 PM, Passing Multiple Proposals

The Shanghai Education Association, with the term of the first board of directors and supervisors having expired, held its second member representative congress at the Municipal People's Education Center yesterday morning from 10:00 AM to discuss important matters and elect directors and supervisors. The Modern Thought Society presented each representative with a volume of books. Details are recorded as follows:

Attendees: Yesterday's attendees included Mayor Wu (represented by Director Pan), Lin Meiyan representing the Municipal Party Headquarters, Jiang Jianbai representing the Municipal Education Bureau, and representatives from various districts: Huang Zao Xiong, Weng Zhi Long, Tao Guang Chuan, Chen Bai, Wang Long Zhang, Chen Ji Cheng, Wang De Yan, Zhang Ji Xin, Cheng Kuan Zheng, Chen Zhong Ji, Feng Yi Xian, Xu Ze Yu, Shen Ding, Wu Chui Jiu, Zhang Zai Bo, Sheng Zhen Sheng, Xu Pei Hang, Wu Ren Qi, and the first board of directors and supervisors: Du Gang, Ma Jia Zhen, and over forty other people.

Meeting Proceedings: The meeting opened at 10:00 AM. The presidium consisted of Du Gang, Zhou Fei Cheng, and Huang Zao Xiong. Wang Long Zhang served as master of ceremonies, and Liu Shun Zai, Zhang Li Chun, and Du Shi Lu served as recorders. After performing the rituals, Chairman Du Gang first reported on the purpose of the meeting, and Huang Zao Xiong reported on the association's work. Subsequently, Director Pan, representing Mayor Wu, Lin Meiyan, representing the Municipal Party Headquarters, and Jiang Jianbai, representing the Municipal Education Bureau, delivered instructions. Elections then followed, and the meeting adjourned for a break at 12:00 PM. The meeting continued at 1:00 PM in the afternoon, discussing proposals and revising the association's constitution. The meeting concluded with a photograph session around 4:00 PM.

Chairman's Report: (1) Du Gang briefly stated that the tasks of today's representative congress can be divided into several points. The Municipal Education Association has been established for two years. According to legal regulations, the term of the directors and supervisors has expired, so today's congress is to elect the second board of directors and supervisors to continue their responsibilities. Secondly, a considerable amount of work has been done during the term of the first board of directors and supervisors, and the appropriateness of this work is subject to review by today's congress. Furthermore, it is hoped that everyone, based on their usual research and involvement in education, or any plans for the future work of the Municipal Education Association, can express their high opinions as much as possible during the discussion, so that the wisdom of all can be gathered to benefit the association. If the Municipal Education Association can have something to follow in the future, it will improve its performance. This is thanks to everyone, and it is also the glory of the Shanghai educational community. (2) Huang Zao Xiong reported that the important work of the association in the past two years includes raising donations to assist the Northeastern Volunteer Army, raising funds for Shanghai school airplanes, publishing the "Shanghai Educational Community," holding summer lectures, holding the "One Yuan Per Month Education Movement," and holding city-wide speeches and competitions on the New Life Movement for primary and secondary school students, etc.

Mayor's Address: Director Pan, representing Mayor Wu, said that the Municipal Education Association is a legal organization. In Shanghai, the administrative aspect of education is the responsibility of the government, while the Municipal Education Association is the only organization promoting it on the social and public fronts. Just now, I heard the chairman's report that a lot of work has been done, but most members have not been able to participate and work together, so the strength has not been fully utilized. It is hoped that this situation will be avoided. The government's finances are tight, and education funds are quite small, and most of them are used in school education. Public education funds account for only 5 percent. This funding is not entirely used for public schools, so the Municipal Education Association launched the One Yuan Per Month Education Movement to supplement the government's inadequate public education and eliminate illiteracy. However, it requires the strength of the entire society to achieve the goal in a short period of time. The One Yuan Per Month Education Movement can enable illiterate people to graduate in four months and learn more than 1,000 characters, costing only four yuan. Among Shanghai's 3.5 million people, there are certainly many illiterate people, but if all members of society can contribute money, illiteracy can be gradually eliminated in three to five years. It is hoped that the Municipal Education Association can continue to do this work consistently, and then it will not be difficult to reduce illiteracy in Shanghai, and it can thus influence the whole country. If education associations in various places do the same, it will not be difficult to eliminate illiteracy throughout the country. It is hoped that everyone will work hard.

Election of Directors and Supervisors: As a result, Huang Zao Xiong, Tao Bai Chuan, Zhou Fei Cheng, Chen Bai, Ma Jia Zhen, Weng Zhi Long, Chen Ji Cheng, Xu Ze Yu, Wu Xiu, Feng Yi Xian, and Zhang Zai Bo were elected as directors. Wang Long Zhang, Wang Tong De, Wu Ru Gui, Wu Ren Qi, and Yang Jing Yi were elected as alternate directors. Du Gang, Jiang Jian Bai, Hao Nai Ding, Chen Zhong Ji, Sheng Zhen Sheng, Cheng Kuan Zheng, and Lin Meiyan were elected as supervisors. Gu Yin Qian and Gu Ji Wu were elected as alternate supervisors.

Discussion of Proposals: (1) Regarding the proposal to vigorously promote the implementation of the association's recommended measures to improve education in the special zone, it was resolved: A. To submit a request to the Municipal Government, the Municipal Education Bureau, and the Municipal Party Headquarters. B. To jointly organize a committee to improve education in the special zone with various organizations. C. To request the Municipal Education Bureau to increase the number of schools or expand the number of classes in the special zone. (2) The proposal to request the Municipal Education Bureau to actively expand rural primary schools to popularize education was approved. (3) The proposal to request the Municipal Education Bureau to reduce or waive tuition fees for rural primary school students as much as possible to broaden education was approved. (4) The proposal to request the Municipal Education Bureau to notify the Municipal Public Utilities Bureau to abolish the school admission advertising tax was approved. (5) The proposal to request the Education Bureau to forward a request to the Municipal Government to increase education funding to 30 percent of the total municipal budget was approved. (6) The proposal to request the Education Bureau to establish a production education experimental school was approved. (7) For the purpose of improving the organization of the Education Association, should district education associations adopt the regulations for holding representative congresses, and can branches be used as basic organizations? It is proposed to request the central government to amend the laws. The proposal was approved. (8) Due to the dense population and high housing prices in the city, it is not easy to obtain large school buildings. The current primary school staffing is uneconomical. Should the Municipal Education Bureau be requested to try the Gary Plan? The proposal was approved. (9) The proposal to amend the draft constitution of the Shanghai Education Association was approved. Finally, supplementary motions: (1) The proposal to request the Municipal Education Bureau to establish a secondary school in the Pu Song District to benefit students was approved. (2) The proposal to suggest that the council of the association prepare a reliable income budget and stipulate that 40 percent of the funds be allocated to the district education associations to facilitate the development of district education associations was approved in principle and referred to the council for consideration. (3) The proposal to request the Municipal Education Bureau to severely punish the principals of the Chuangshi, Dajiang, Shihuadongya, and Fourth Schools who absconded with funds to serve as a warning was approved. All the above approved cases were handed over to the council for handling.

Establishment of the Chinese Stenography Association

The Chinese Stenography Association, organized by stenographers of various styles, has been in preparation for two months and is now ready. It held its inaugural meeting yesterday (the 21st) at 9:00 AM at the Juvenile Propaganda Troupe, and discussed the association's constitution and elected officers. Details are recorded as follows:

Members Present: In addition to Director Pan of the Municipal Education Bureau and representative Nie Haifan, and Wang Longzhang representing the Municipal Party Headquarters, who attended to provide guidance, the members present included Xue Guangqian, Xu Xingchu, Chen Dongbai, Zhu Zhiming, Zhu Zhongzheng, Huang Pengnian, Yang Zhenzhong, Cai Zhaolian, He Zhen, Xue Jianxin, Zhu Rongting, Wang Gongxia, Sun Zuxun, Liu Dihua, Gu Junquan, Luo Zhenkai, Feng Song, Wu Renhao, Qi Mengfei, Lai Zhiwen, Zhu Xiaochun, Xue Fengshen, Wang Zhaohou, Jin Shou, Jiang Da, Mao Yong, Zhu Jinwu, Liu Baihen, Bu Gangjian, Li Shilin, Tong Yikang, and over sixty other people.

Meeting Proceedings: The meeting opened at 9:00 AM. The presidium consisted of Yang Zhenzhong, Xu Xingchu, and Zhu Yongzheng. The preparatory committee consisted of Zhu Zhiming, Chen Dongbai, Cai Zhaolian, and Huang Pengnian. Qi Mengfei served as master of ceremonies, and Jiang Da served as recorder. After performing the rituals, Chairman Xu Xingchu first delivered the opening address, and Zhu Zhongzheng reported on the preparatory process. Subsequently, Director Pan, Wang Longzhang representing the Municipal Party Headquarters, and Nie Haifan representing the Municipal Education Bureau, delivered instructions. Then, the association's constitution was discussed and proposals were passed. Finally, officers were elected, a photograph was taken, and the meeting adjourned.

Proposals Passed: Chairman Yang Zhenzhong first discussed the association's constitution, amending it item by item, and it was passed in its entirety. Then, the following proposals were discussed: (1) To hold Chinese stenography training courses to cultivate stenography professionals. (2) To hold stenography academic lectures. (3) To publish publications within the association's economic capabilities to promote stenography academic studies. (4) To compile various styles of stenography and edit a stenography yearbook. It was resolved that the above proposals be submitted to the council for discussion and handling.

Election of Directors: The directors were elected. Wang Longzhang representing the Municipal Party Headquarters and Nie Haifan representing the Municipal Education Bureau supervised the election. As a result, Xu Xingchu, Xue Guangqian, Chen Dongbai, Zhu Zhiming, Huang Pengnian, Feng Song, Zhu Zhongzheng, He Zhen, and Wu Renhao were elected as directors. It is reported that a council meeting will be convened soon to allocate responsibilities.

Datong University Invited He Yingqin and Chen Lifu to Speak Yesterday

He Spoke on How to Restore a Good Scholarly Atmosphere

Chen Spoke on the Scientific Analysis of Propriety, Justice, Integrity, and Shame

Since implementing national rejuvenation education last year, Datong University has spared no effort in fostering a frugal scholarly atmosphere, promoting academic research, and dedicating itself to hard work. This semester, the implementation of universal physical education and a universal tutor system has achieved remarkable results. The university also invites prominent figures to speak during memorial week to provide inspiration. Yesterday morning at 11:00 AM, the university invited trustee He Yingqin to speak on "How to Restore a Good Scholarly Atmosphere." At 2:00 PM in the afternoon, it invited Central Committee member Chen Lifu to speak on "A Scientific Analysis of Propriety, Justice, Integrity, and Shame." All faculty, staff, and students attended the lectures, and the atmosphere was extremely enthusiastic. The main points of the speeches are summarized as follows:

He Yingqin's speech on how to restore a good scholarly atmosphere was divided into five key points: First, to ensure that young people in schools develop a spirit of sacrificing for the country and the nation. Second, to strictly require teachers and students to work hard in their respective positions. Third, to find ways to make teachers and students cooperate closely. Fourth, to make school life and social life adaptable. Fifth, to pay attention to physical education and military training, and to encourage Datong University to transform into a new scholarly atmosphere, burying itself in hard work, hard teaching, and hard learning, in preparation for the rejuvenation of the nation and the strengthening of the country.

Chen Lifu's speech on the scientific analysis of propriety, justice, integrity, and shame first argued from the perspective of wisdom, benevolence, and courage. To determine the four cardinal principles is in the hand of wisdom, to implement the four cardinal principles is in the realm of courage, and to know the principles and principles of the four cardinal principles is in the realm of benevolence. Respect and love are born from wisdom, benevolence, and courage. Respect for others is propriety, and respect for oneself is integrity. Love for others is justice, and love for oneself is shame. From an economic perspective, propriety and integrity are distribution, and justice and shame are production. Speaking of the objects of the four cardinal principles, propriety is for others, justice is for things, integrity is for objects, and shame is for oneself. Chen cited extensively, with both solemnity and humor. The entire audience applauded and cheered, gaining a powerful inspiration for the New Life Movement.

Chen Lifu also gave a speech at the School of Business yesterday. Central Committee member Chen Lifu arrived in Shanghai at 7:20 AM yesterday morning on an overnight express train from Beijing. After getting off the train, he went directly to the National Shanghai School of Business to participate in the memorial week and gave a speech on "A Scientific Explanation of Propriety, Justice, Integrity, and Shame." He also encouraged the students of the school. Chen intends to stay in Shanghai for a day or two to deal with private affairs before returning to Beijing.

Minister Trautmann believes that if human beings only pursue the development of industry and neglect rationality and ethical connections, not only will they not be able to reduce the degree of disputes in the current world, but they may also make the differences between ethnic groups more obvious. Therefore, after the European War, various countries are striving to refresh their national life, eliminate class contradictions, and concentrate power. This is not only true for European countries, but also for China. The current New Life Movement and the Confucian Movement can serve as clear evidence. After Minister Tao finished speaking, the principal of the school, Weng Zhilong, expressed his gratitude, and the guests and hosts dispersed happily. Qian Xing Su and Others' Performance Record at the Nanchang Women's Games

Excellent Performance Highly Welcomed in Jiangxi

Nanchang's First Women's Games Conclude Successfully

(Nanchang Correspondent from Shen Shi News Agency) The first Provincial Women's Games were held on the 14th, 15th, and 16th at the Provincial Public Sports Field. Participants included ten girls' schools: Girls' High School, Girls' Vocational School, Baoling School, Jiansheng Midwifery School, Jiangxi Middle School, Second Vocational School, First Middle School, Tianhou Palace Elementary School, and the Court Elementary School. Director Cheng of the Education Department, the president of the Games, in order to promote women's sports in the province and to allow for more observation, specially invited twelve female track and field athletes, including Qian Xing Su, who are renowned throughout the country from the Shanghai East Asia Physical Education School, to come to Jiangxi for a performance. After receiving the invitation, Ms. Qian and the others, led by Chen Mengyu, the principal of East Asia School, and Ms. Li Huaifen, the disciplinarian of the school's women's division, arrived as scheduled. They performed in the field every day, achieving astonishing results, giving the women of Jiangxi Province a very deep impression, and greatly promoting the future development of sports in various girls' schools. The process is recorded below.

Qian Xing Su and Her Group Arrive in the Province After departing from Shanghai, Qian Xing Su and her group from the Shanghai East Asia Physical Education School arrived in the province by train from Xunyang on the 12th. The organizing committee sent representatives Li Zonghao and Liang Yaoting to meet them at the station. At about 12:00 noon, Ms. Qian and her group arrived at the station. Li and others led them across the river and went directly to the Provincial Nanchang Girls' Middle School in Songbai Lane to rest. Those who came with Ms. Qian included team leader Li Huaifen, and team members Chen Shuqing, Chen Wanqing, Wang Huachang, Xue Zhengxia, Xu Yuan, Qin Chiming, Wang Yuying, Pan Jingxian, Pan Gui, Sun Ruiying, and Jiang Yuanying, totaling twelve people, as well as Principal Chen Mengyu.

The Opening Ceremony Was Very Solemn The opening ceremony of the Games was held at 9:00 am on the 14th. Over a thousand people attended, including President Cheng Shiwei, Central Committee member Ding Chaowu, Provincial Executive Committee members Wang Guanying and Yu Baiqing, Provincial Government member Li Dezhao, guests from all walks of life, female students from various schools, athletes, and Games staff. After performing the ceremony, President Cheng reported on the purpose of the meeting, followed by speeches from Ding Chaowu, Yu Baiqing, Chen Mengyu, and others. Then, athlete representative Ms. Zhao Zhongying took the oath. When the Games song was sung, the sound of "strive, strive" filled the air, and the atmosphere of the entire field was very solemn. Then, there was a parade. Accompanied by sports music, the participants circled the field three times. The competition then began. Although the performances in various events were relatively immature, the performance by Qian Xing Su and others on the field greatly stimulated the excitement of the competitors.

Two Performances Amazed the Audience After the second program on the first day of the Games, the Shanghai ladies participated in the 50-meter performance. The participants were Qian Xing Su, Chen Shuqing, Chen Wanqing, Wang Yuying, and Xu Yuan. After the starting gun fired, the five ladies started running. Before reaching twenty meters, Ms. Chen Shuqing took the lead, while Ms. Qian fell behind. The audience thought that Ms. Qian would definitely fail this time. Unexpectedly, Ms. Qian straightened her chest and sprinted forward like an arrow. When she reached the finish line, she had already won by a chest's length, turning defeat into victory. The audience applauded and cheered. Her time was 6.8 seconds. The highest score in the competition that day was 7.6 seconds, a vast difference. When the 80-meter low hurdle preliminary was completed, Qian and Ms. Wang Huachang performed hurdle jumping. Qian's hurdle jumping skills were very skilled, and her posture was excellent. Each time she crossed a hurdle, she rose and fell gracefully, dazzling the audience. Soon, the two had crossed the last hurdle and were about to reach the finish line. At that time, Qian was still behind Wang, and the audience couldn't help but sweat for her. However, Qian increased her speed and still won by a line. Her time was 14.6 seconds.

Relay Performance Astonishes the Audience On the second day of the Games (15th), although the autumn wind and rain brought a sudden drop in temperature, the East Asia athletes still performed. However, the performance was greatly affected by the weather. (1) Qian Xing Su ran 100 meters in 14 seconds exactly. (2) Ms. Wang Huachang, Xu Yuan, and Pan Jingxian did the high jump. Wang was first with a score of 1.29 meters. Her posture was very good. (3) Afterwards, Qian Xing Su, Xu Yuan, Wang Huachang, and Chen Shuqing performed the 400-meter relay, accompanied by the Girls' Middle School team. At that time, there was drizzling rain and a cold wind. After the starting gun fired, Chen Shuqing set off first, followed by Wang Huachang and Xu Yuan. Qian Xing Su was the last person. After receiving the baton, Qian sprinted like lightning with a composed posture. When she reached the finish line, the Girls' Middle School team was still more than 80 meters away. The time was 55 seconds exactly. The entire audience was amazed.

Basketball Performance Amazes with Skill On the third day of the Games (16th), the East Asia team's basketball performance was one of the most exciting scenes. The audience gathered, surrounding the entire basketball court. The East Asia players stepped onto the court amidst cheers. In the first half, they competed with East Asia alumni (male students), displaying a hundred brilliant moves, leaving the audience in admiration. The result was a score of 10 to 10. In the second half, they competed with the Women's Games champion team (Girls' Vocational School), resulting in a one-sided situation. The Girls' Vocational School players paled in comparison. The result was East Asia 29 points, and Girls' Vocational School only 3 points.

General Impression is Very Deep This time, Qian Xing Su and her group of more than ten people came to Jiangxi to perform, leaving all parties with the following profound impressions: (1) Their clothing and lifestyle were very simple and frugal, costing only five or six hundred yuan, less than a quarter of what Yang Xiuqiong spent last time. (2) Qian and the others were honest and kind, and their knowledge was also very valuable. They were not overly modern or urbanized. (3) Ms. Qian's calligraphy was very beautiful, and her Mandarin speeches were clear, logical, and pleasant to listen to. This truly caused most dignitaries to express their respect.

Spring and Autumn

Little Western Paradise

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 3 Unraveling, Zero Peering Door Pitiful Girl, Willing to Hear Hardships Cherishing Jade Visits Home

He held a thin straw hat in one hand, slowly fanning his chest, and carried a large string of mutton in the other, humming a Shaanxi tune and walking slowly past. When he walked past, he only glanced at the workers, and immediately the noisy sounds of the entire field completely stopped. Cheng Zhiqian looked at the man, then at the workers, and when the fat man walked far away, he couldn't help but smile at the workers: Who was that person who just passed by? I see you are all a little afraid of him. A worker smiled and replied: That's our boss, how can we not be afraid? Sir, have you eaten yet? Cheng Zhiqian said: You eat very hard! The worker sighed: This is nothing compared to our hometown, that's when it's hard! You people who work as teachers, how would you know? Cheng Zhiqian laughed: Some know, some don't, but I'm thinking, if it's harder than this, then you can only eat coarse grains. The craftsman seemed to think that he was too amateurish and smiled at his companion next to him. Cheng Zhiqian realized that he had misspoke, which was a little embarrassing. So he joked and laughed: I heard that you have dug a few cave dwellings here, where are they? A worker pointed to the back and said: Isn't that there? Cheng Zhiqian followed the direction he was pointing. In the back of the courtyard, there was a two-foot-high brick wall, like a flower stand, or like a fence around a pool. He immediately walked forward to see that at the corner of the short wall, there was an opening with layers of steps to walk down. Indeed, a very long and deep pit was dug into the ground, forming an aisle. On the south side of the aisle, earth was used as a screen wall. On the north side of the aisle, a dam was built, and doors and windows were dug, a row of five or six rooms, just like houses. (46)

A Look at Life Then and Now

— Chen Jingyu

Living in this current era, who isn't complaining about "the difficulty of life!" Indeed, the difficulty of life has now reached its extreme and has become an undeniable fact. Compared to the "Qianlong" and "Jiaqing" years of the previous Qing Dynasty, there is a vast difference, not to be mentioned in the same breath! In the eyes of today, the life of the people at that time can really be considered as heavenly gods, achieved after several lifetimes of cultivation! If you don't believe me, there is a book to prove it.

Yesterday, I happened to be airing books in the sun and found a book by Mr. Lin Qin'nan, "Miscellaneous Records of Tieqiao Pavilion." After reading it through, there is the following record:

"During the "Qianlong" and "Jiaqing" periods of the previous Qing Dynasty, Fujian was extremely frugal. City dwellers were like villagers. Those who hired sedan chairs charged forty coins for ten miles. Prostitutes lived in low houses, and one night with them cost thirty-six coins. My friend Ding Tanghao, who was humorous, once said to me: "In the past, there was a prodigal who could enjoy wine, meat, and rice, and prostitute, gamble, and hire a sedan chair for no more than one hundred coins!" I said: 'Please tell me the details?' Ding said: 'Hiring a sedan chair from the South Gate to Jiangnan Bridge costs forty coins. There is a shop on the bridge that sells japonica rice and meat for thirteen coins. A large cup of wine costs six coins. One night with a prostitute costs only thirty-six coins. There are still five coins left, three coins for a small gamble, and the winnings are pebbles. With the remaining two coins, he buys a torch to enter the city at dusk, which is just under one hundred coins! And all evils are prepared!'" I laughed loudly!' - Note that there is a separate edition of this book now, but this article has been deleted.

After reading these miscellaneous records, can one not admire the ease of the lives of the ancients and lament that I was not born at the right time? A prodigal's daily expenses like this, if compared to the current standard of living, is not even one or two percent of it. Therefore, considering those people as 'heavenly gods, achieved after several lifetimes of cultivation' cannot be considered reckless or exaggerated, right?

Tidbits

— (Shui'e)

The city is a cage made of gold thread, imprisoning a large group of self-satisfied birds.

Experience is a good book for people, but good books are only reference books for people.

You only feel the preciousness of money when you have spent the last few of it.

The Mandarin Duck Score

— Chifo

Recently, there was an interesting advertisement in the newspaper. The picture shows ten young men and ten young women, each holding a string. These twenty strings are combined and tied to the hands of the old man under the moon in the clouds. On each string are written the surnames of these twenty young men and women, tied together in pairs, secretly hidden in the hands of the old man under the moon. These will be the predetermined couples in the future, called "The Mandarin Duck Score." This advertisement is for readers to guess, and those who guess correctly will receive fragrant gifts such as mandarin duck pillows.

This novel game is really very interesting; it's a pity that we are not the old man under the moon, and I'm afraid that if we were to play the role of Magistrate Qiao, we would inevitably make a mess of the mandarin duck score, and not only would we not get mandarin duck pillows, but we would be afraid of being beaten by the old man under the moon.

Is the union of husband and wife really in the power of the old man under the moon? In the current era, the union of the two sexes is not only beyond the control of the old and confused old man under the moon, but also the biological parents have no control! Perhaps the old man under the moon has already resigned and retired to the mountains and forests with his old wife. The responsibility of tying the red string has been handed over to the "God of Wealth Bodhisattva."

The allusion to the old man under the moon comes from "Supplementary Records of the Strange and Mysterious." According to legend, "Wei Gu of the Tang Dynasty was staying at a shop south of Song City when he saw an old man examining books under the moon. Gu asked what book it was. The old man said: 'It is the marriage register of the world.' He entered the rice market and saw a blind old woman holding a three-year-old girl. The old man pointed and said: 'This is your wife.' Gu was angry and gave a small knife to a servant to kill the girl. The servant stabbed her in the crowd and ran away. Fourteen years later, Wang Tai, the prefect of Xiangzhou, married his daughter, who had a beautiful appearance and always wore a flower on her eyebrow. Gu asked about it. She said: 'When I was an infant, my wet nurse, Chen, took me to the market and was stabbed by a mad thief. The scar is still there.' Gu said: 'Is Chen blind?' She said: 'Yes.' He then recounted the previous event and was filled with awe. When the magistrate of Song City heard about it, he inscribed the shop with the name "Marriage Shop." This is certainly a myth, and in the past era of "marrying a chicken and following the chicken, marrying a dog and following the dog," it was indeed a wonderful method of consolation. Nowadays, if there is an old man under the moon, he would not have the patience to pull these messy and tangled red strings.

Heavy

Water Pipe

— Xia Cenjuan

A water pipe is also called a water tobacco pouch, or a water tobacco tube. Although it is called a water pipe, it is not only used to smoke Lanzhou water tobacco. Anything from leather silk, pure silk, to the old tobacco smoked by the old uncles in the countryside can be smoked. There are three kinds of changes in the structure of the water pipe. The first kind is commonly known as the seedling pipe, which has a simple form and is more than a foot long. It is not only unsightly but also very inconvenient to hold in the hand while smoking. This kind of pipe existed as early as sixty or seventy years ago. Now it can be said to be extremely rare. The second type is improved to be small and exquisite, and the third type is even better, called a spray pipe. What is a spray pipe? Because the tobacco butt left over from smoking in an ordinary pipe must be blown out after removing the pipe head, the spray pipe does not require this trouble. You only need to raise the pipe head slightly, and the tobacco butt will be blown out. When cigarettes had not yet appeared, the water pipe also occupied a necessary position in the household. Regardless of whether they were rich or poor, every family had one or two of them. If distinguished guests arrived, in addition to fragrant tea, the water pipe had to be respectfully offered. Even if the guest did not smoke water tobacco, they would accept it to put on airs. Therefore, in the past, there was a profession in teahouses for filling water pipes. It is said that even in the Shanghai brothels, they would fill the water pipe for their lovers to smoke.

Since the prevalence of cigarettes, the water pipe has been overthrown and has become the end of its rope. The fate of the water pipe was almost at an end. Fortunately, there are still some elderly people who still use water pipes to smoke, maintaining its original position. Therefore, the shops that sell water pipes sigh there every day. If they do not sell other things, they will almost have to tighten their belts and drink the northwest wind. This is also one of the vicissitudes of commerce.

This year, the government advocates the New Life Movement, and the word thrift also occupies an important part. Therefore, I quit cigarettes and switched to smoking water tobacco. The results after a month are very surprising, because the cigarette expenses that originally cost about five yuan a month now cost less than one yuan a month for water tobacco. Moreover, cigarettes contain the toxin nicotine, but there is no toxin at all when smoking with a water pipe. It is economical and hygienic, so why not do it? With some feelings, I remembered the water pipe again. I write this to tell the people who smoke cigarettes.

Drifting Fragrance from the Imperial Incense

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

When we first left Shanhaiguan, most of what we saw was still plains. After passing Xinmin, the population became extraordinarily sparse, and many mountains, both high and low, gradually appeared around us. These mountains were mostly branches of a certain small mountain range, some very close to the tracks and some very far away, but none possessed any magnificent wonders. Only in the distance to the west could we vaguely see a very long mountain range, with peaks high into the clouds, overlapping each other. At this time, our imperial train was just moving forward in that direction, so the closer we got, the more it changed from a faint ink-like line, gradually turning gray, and then turning blue - a very lovely color of blue. But in fact, it was still very far away from us.

As I was concentrating on admiring the distant mountain scenery, I suddenly felt that there seemed to be a kind of disturbance on our imperial train. Although no one was jumping and running around, and no one was making loud noises, the order was no longer as neat as before. I couldn't help but be surprised, so I quickly asked a companion, and learned that our train would not go directly to Fengtian. At the station before Fengtian, Huanggu Village, it would stop, and for the rest of the journey, we would no longer rely on the snail-paced train, but would change to the official sedan chairs that we were used to.

Now that I knew that we would be getting off the train soon, I had no intention to look at the scenery anymore. And in fact, there was nothing special to see in the short distance we passed through at this time that was worth admiring. (156)

Small Recipes

###濟南蒲菜

— 南宮生

In the seasons of summer and autumn, from after the Dragon Boat Festival in May to the Double Ninth Festival in September, the freshest and most popular vegetable dish in the entire city of Jinan, Shandong, is called Pu Cai. Anyone who has been to Jinan and spent the summer and autumn there probably cannot help but think of how fresh and clean the flavor of Pu Cai is.

The shape of Pu Cai is somewhat similar to the wild rice shoots of the South, but it is absolutely white and tender. Among all vegetables, it is probably a top-tier one that can be compared. Even the most famous Bian Sun (bamboo shoots) from Hangzhou are inferior to Pu Cai. The wonderful taste can be imagined. Pu Cai can be cooked in various ways, such as braised in soy sauce or stir-fried plain. It can be stir-fried with shredded meat or mixed with dried tofu. However, the most famous dish in Jinan is Milk Soup Pu Cai. The fresh juices of meat and fish are used to cook a white soup that looks like milk. The Pu Cai is then cooked in the soup. This becomes a famous dish of Jinan, with a unique flavor. Seeing the fresh, milky-white soup and the incredibly tender Pu Cai, everyone can imagine the deliciousness of this dish and cannot help but have their appetites stirred.

What exactly is this Pu Cai? It is actually the cattail grass that grows in Daming Lake in Jinan. During the transition from summer to autumn, it is in its freshest and most tender period. The white and tender section is harvested and becomes this delicious vegetable dish. In Shanghai and other places, Western restaurants often use canned asparagus, which is an imported product. This is the same as Pu Cai. During the summer and autumn seasons, when Pu Cai is fresh and tender, it is purchased, cooked, and packaged into cans, then sold back to the Chinese market. However, its price has already increased tenfold. The Chinese people only know that this canned asparagus is a delicacy among vegetables, but they do not know its origin is Pu Cai. Just between this export and import, the leakage of wealth is immeasurable.

Among the products exported from Daming Lake in Jinan, the most abundant is Pu Cai. In addition to being cooked locally when it is in season, there are countless people who purchase it to make canned asparagus. Therefore, the production of Pu Cai in Daming Lake in Jinan is always around one million yuan each year. The main sales channel is as the raw material for making asparagus. If the quantity of asparagus imported and sold each year is compared with the quantity of Pu Cai produced, there is an annual loss of tens of thousands of yuan.

When Pu Cai becomes old in winter and spring, it can be cut down and made into Pu Bao (cattail bags). The Pu Bao used everywhere in the market for packaging items is made from old Pu Cai, which can be considered a by-product of Pu Cai.

Most Chinese people only know how to stick to the old ways and do not think about creating new things. This naturally produced Pu Cai has so many uses and can be made into asparagus. Why not set up our own factories to process it, instead of letting other people take all the profits with a simple effort? If we can utilize this natural product and establish our own factories to produce asparagus, selling it throughout the country, it may be a way to stop the leakage of wealth.
